When belly solution comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues which is in the stomach and in the intestine is weakened, and cannot be cured by means of cures; and you see the patient suffering much and of great virtue, then do one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before about the cautery of the stomach, to the circulating cautery; and four cauteries around the navel subtle, at each cautery a subtle cleaver, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the humors abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are in their foundation, or one or more, and they are old and are of large humors cold and moist corrupted, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit at all, if you make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is all outside below the scapula point to point in a triangle, and one cautery below the buttock two fingers.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face one makes i. great cautery on the stomach, as it has been said before, and one other on the liver, and one other on the mice to all the cautery clavile; and leave the cautery open long time. After cure the place as long as it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul," sharpen the cautery which seems like i. razor, and then put it all ablaze on that "thelul"  cut; and let it there as long as the cauteries reach the birth of the vein, so that the blood does not clot; do this once or twice, and if there is much "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of ointments beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the "alchatim," it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will relate in its place, such a malady comes that it can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to any [place], and is filled with corruption and putrid moisture, then take a subtle probe, and carefully know how far the probe has entered. Then heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe entered, and continue the cautery until the corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of need; and beware of burning the nerves which are inside, and the large veins. If the fistula goes toward the bladder and intestines, then beware of those places, and do not perform this outside [of] fleshy areas, and think that it is not passed through; after healing the place until it is sound, and if the place is healed and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the place is troubled, and the bones at the root are corrupted; and in this way like those which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes as rains, and of great windiness, and does not take much of a woman, then it is necessary that you make cautery on the loins on one side and the other with the cautery clavicle that we have said before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will do more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and feeble from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then I make cautery in the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the groin begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as our finger; and I make one cautery outside the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be clavicle according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for those to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the bud, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cauteries be clavil, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the bone of the hip, and for this cause it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and it is found the level of the viscus department, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the bone of the hip with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the place around the bone as it turns, so that the bone be inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as the one with which the stomach was cauterized.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present to you, make .iij. cauteries of the olive large, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and cure it until it is sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the socket of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of those things that we have said in the division and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that you make cautery; and the manner of the cautery is in two ways: namely, both ardent medicines and fire cautery. Fire cautery is in many ways, some of which are such: that you cauterize on the socket of the hip three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them with a good depth and width, and have between each cautery a space the size of a digit, and let the cauteries be olive; sometimes one makes cautery in the middle on the top of the hip, for which reason there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see it, cauterize it with the cautery of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do in such a manner that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the spaces of the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which it is done in sciatica, when pain holds in the hip, and does not reach to the thigh nor the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, then one makes .ii. cauteries there where the patient says that the pain holds him, and .i. cautery above the ankle 4 fingers, to the left side a little; and let the cauteries be pointed, and let the spaces of the heart be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to 2 fingers of the foot or near it, then one cauterizes where he feels the pain .iij. points or .iiij. with the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, then one does more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, then one makes a cautery with the pointed or circular cautery; and well guard in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so much that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do no more nuisance and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen more than a few who had cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was all swollen, and the foot as well, and it became pierced and corrupt throughout the foot. After a solution of belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and the other, according to this manner. // And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, for that reason here is the manner, make one such iron and be at the head as thick as a thumb nail, or a little less, and be between grooves and be from one groove to the other of spacing the quantity of a finger's knuckle; and let the grooves be toward two parts, and let them also be like knuckles, and there be one handle of iron well made; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and feel its heat, and then put it on the bone of the diseased hip, and be turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once one cautery return and leave it three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regard, and we see few who use it; and nonetheless these are good cauteries, which can bear it, and where it is needed.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or from percussion or by excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter spread, none of these appearances are worth cautery except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be void of fetid pills or other similar things, that on him be made upon his back, where the pain holds, three lines signed with inche, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make .iij. cauteries or .iiij. at the clavile cautery mean according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight belly when they cry, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this kind according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery grazes each part of the spine evenly. And if you see it, cauterize around the spine with the poignant cautery two or three lines, and let the points be near each other. After curing the place until it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not administer cautery in a cavity which is in a nerve spame.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is from moisture that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, that which they call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make the fire cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the foot, then make cautery to the whole cautery which one calls "point." And if the pains come as far as the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make cautery on each knee three or four cauteries of each part, to all the olive-shaped cautery; and if you have need of more, then make more, but do not hold your hand there further than while the head of the fire is burning.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then administer the cautery that we have said in our chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines; and if there remains no pain at the elbows, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and make good governance for the sick person and ponder medicines. For if you make good governance for him and purge phlegm, then he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes in the arms, and the tendons descend to the elbows, it is newly, so when you see him cured, that he does not move it on that day; and that he uses things that hold up his belly, so that the fibers descend from his belly; after that make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm as long as the tendons are repaired, and straighten them towards your thumbs, and sign of a circle under the rupture on the bone of the shoulder, and with a whole sign that is similar to half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of this which is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and he feels the heat. Then straighten the tendons to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so that they do not return backwards; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him one cushion and one sergeant on the thighs, and one other on the leg which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your strength, and hold it straight and keep it there until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again once more until you come to the bone; and be careful that the tendon does not protrude when you make the cautery; that you do not burn it; and so that by this the patient does not die, or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And knows that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your works are worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of bones, and of big people also big according to their measure; after .iij. days cure their place with butter until the burning is removed; after the cure of other ointments until it is healed, and lies the patient .xl. days on his back until the wound is well joined; and it is necessary that his dressings be long, so that the boil does not come out when he tries to go into chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after .xl. days, when he wants to get up, if it is administered a good splint, and wear it for another .xl. days; and have good rest, that he does not work much and beware of too much repletion of drinking and eating, and of too high braiding; and when he does this teaching, it is healed entirely. And I will say here after the cure of tailoring in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then you make one cautery with the cautery according to its quantity, and after curing according to what we have said; and none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first sign the place of the rupture and make a line through the width above the rupture, and another one outside, and keep your hand in all the cautery clamp. But the first cauteries are lighter and more mobile.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from a fall or striking, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twists and its pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, it is well; if not, start again another cautery on top of that one, because it is customary that it must change in the member that is nearest to it, for which reason it is necessary that you do the cauteries as long as the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The surgeons are aided at times by cautery with great help, and also for the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see them being cauterized, take note if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not increase or remain, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the patient, then do five cauteries on the head: one above the head, and the other towards the front near the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the back. And let your hand stay so that the cautery comes right up to the bone, and so that the bark is pushed out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize on the mice according to how it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mesentery is spread everywhere; and it manifests clearly, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and one cautery on its navel, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one great one on the crupie and one other under, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the arms, and two on the tendons of the hip, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard against the nerves that are on the last calf, that you do not burn them; and sometimes it is done cauterizing on the bone of the arm, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when more cauteries are made, the more help is done, and the more it profits; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cautery as healthy people feel it, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it behooves the cauteries to be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in ways of irons. After cure the place with flour of wheat with honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes in any limb and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size and the smallness of the limb; and let the cautery be one prick entering into the thickness of the flesh; then cure with ointment until it is healed. And sometimes one makes cautery on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus is removed the swelling; and nonetheless do not interfere any who is not knowledgeable of the limbs and of the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	from girdles
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the malady that is called "albaras" is present, and the means of medicine avail nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery one prick through, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, until the blemish is removed, and its color changed; then cure with flour of vicees and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alondre, of each one part; and mix all together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of sores by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a sore begins and you wish to arrest it, cauterize it with the cautery which seems like .i. circle, all around the border of the sore.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has a disease that is called "adubelati," and it tarries to die, or because of the superfluity that it makes, or because of the water of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you want to hasten its death: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries in pricking; afterwards leave it so. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce with all the cautery, so heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" as long as the cautery pierces the core, and be such the cautery that the patient feels it from outside in such a manner that the course of the rot is alleviated. After the cure as long as it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another manner of disease there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else than a consumption of the limb, because it consumes the limbs as fire does the dry vines. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer cauterization with fire, then sharpen the iron cautery quite small and large, according to what is fitting for the place where the disease is; after, cauterize all around until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing of it remains, that all that which is corrupt be removed. And then leave it for 3 days, and put on the cauterized places softened broil with oil as long as the scabs of fire are removed, and all the corruption. After the cure of suppuration generating flesh.  And if you see after 3 days that healthy flesh does not rise, it is good; and if this one, then begin the cautery again on what remains of the corrupt places. And this consumption has been cured at times with ague medicine in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of ague medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the  sprouts which come to the foot
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that to the foot by fire there is born a malady which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing feared which bleaches the foot. And the cautery of this malady si is in .ij. manners. That is to say cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. The cautery of fire si is that you heat one cautery like as it is a penne of vulture, and be made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the nail on all sides, and that it have subtle margins; after put it all hot upon the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it so for .iij. days until it begins to get rotten; then make an ointment of wild mallows ground with oil, and leave the ointment upon all night, and the nails will fall and will be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment, inciting flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by fire the body, and many times happen and in hands and in feet, si it is necessary that you bring them cautery of hot water; and it is in this manner: take a cane of iron or of fer, or a penne of vulture, and put upon the nail and the althelul, that is to say sprouts warts; and put the cane above so that it penetrates all around, then I put a pot of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water way deep until the root; and suffer the patient a little the biting of the hot water an hour; then leave it so, and it will be uprooted all at all its roots. Thus make one after another, as long as you eradicate all those who are in the body, then cure them with ointments which inciting flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or fever quartan or other, so it befits that you make to him .iv. cauteries or .iii. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each spine; and .i. cautery or weight, and .i. on the stomach at the olive cautery; so will leave the trembling, and hastens the saint health from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	of festering pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes appear by fire on the body baths, or festering pustules, that come from large corrupt matters. So it befits at first when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle twig, so that its point is seized with fire, or from root of long arisologe, or to the lentil cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they may not grow in them afterward, but are broken the superfluities whence they come, and are healed; but it befits that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great spurts of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nonetheless when this happens to anyone, quickly put your finger on the wound of the vein, and restrain it very tightly until the bleeding is appeased under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put to fire the olive cauteries more small and large as much as they are all red; then take one, or a great one or a small one according to the wound and its place where the artery is routed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily one other of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these one after the other until the vein is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve which is beside it, and that another malice does not come upon the patient; and know that when a vein departs from the artery, one cannot well stretch it, even when the artery is great, unless by one of the four manners that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding of thread, or by medicines put upon it which have power to stretch veins; and be bound and restrained well.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring a stretching of ligaments tightly by straps or by putting things burning on it, or other similar things, if it does not profit to this?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no medicine present, then he should put his right index finger upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until it is stretched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but often wet with cold water so that it be very cold until the vein is congealed and thickened and stretched; and make from then on those things which he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures of the tail
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the maladies in which it is necessary cautery of fire, or ardent medicine, and the incisions and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have put that chapter from the head jus to the foot, and I will go in this chapter by that same way for those who find it more easily what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear pupil, that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of cauteries, and for that reason it is necessary more great caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly. Because many kinds of people come to cures. Some come with such illnesses that they die easily because of the frenzy that they find in their illness, and because of the greatness of their wickedness; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is deceitful. It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more care in your honor than in your greed, and do not open foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain about, and whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and memory of length.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, May our Lords give you good understanding and rightness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter to you in devising by chapters, according to those that it is before or chapter of cauteries, which I have devised from the chief to foot, for those that you find more easily those that you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes many times to children at birth, and when the midwife strains too hard the head of the child; and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and to all those that I have seen it has hastened death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is better for me to leave the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose shoulder was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until he could not support it; and he thought so much because of the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and the work is like this if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you split in the middle of the head a wide fissure; and be also long as two fingers, as much as the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more thick, and the abscess is larger, do two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see the commissures of the shoulder open on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inward, and this does not return to you: then it behooves you to split in the middle of the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision extract the moisture all out. After extract the incisions of cloths and powders, and put wine and oil there, and let so until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound by tents and by ointments, and leave to be restrained the chief bandage, and then feed the patient dry meat of lack of moisture as long as the limb be strengthened and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where opens the greatness of the abscess, and its assembly of water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess opens, and its filling of water, and  cut it according to what you have power; and guard that you do not cut the artery; and vein blood flows, so that the patient dies from the decrease of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of summary
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a sickness that is called “catarrh” at the eyes or at the chest, and the patient is old, and the cure of medicine does not profit, then the last cure is the cautery with those one covers the 2 arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It then behooves you, when you see them to cover, that the patient make back his head; after he rubs their place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then binds the patient's neck with one cloth; then look where the vein beats, and their positions of the one and the other are after the ears, and so are placed; then sign their locations with ink, then cover both with a sharp spatula of 2 parts. as far as the flesh comes to the bone, and this is by the broad side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, plunge the spatula under the artery and cover it above, cutting also as 2 fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood jumps out continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then you must measure the quantity of space of three digits, then sign it and make it up to the bone; and that which is needed to put out the blood is six c., and perhaps a bit more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone without any sheath, then cut it so that no abscess comes, then restrain the wound and bind it, and the care of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When a chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moistures of tears and the heats in the temples and the old soreness and similar things, and it is medicated by ways of medicine and all that does not help him, then restrain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes rear the hairs of his temples, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is poorly returned outwards than in some men who are too cold; and if it is returned, it strains the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then trace it upwards as much as possible with pincers, and depart well from the nets that are beneath on each side; and if the artery is thin, turn it back at the point of the needle, then cut that part according to the quantity of two chias. For if it is not cut, it does not jump out completely in every way.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the six to three; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two leagues of a strong double silk thread, so that rotting does not come before the soldering of the wound, and there comes bleeding; then cut the superfluity which is between the two liens in the same hour, and then, if you see fit, you cauterize it with a cuticular cautery until the bones are reached as long as the chias are cut; and this is the middle work, if the patient has no fever and he is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is an aid to finish the moistures: for this reason it is of greater help to moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill their place with old cotton and put on them tents well made; and when they are undone, let there be care with dry medicines which make flesh grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if without a stop of the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten to cover by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and restrain it to your hand that the bleeding cease; and if you lack these present things, put on the place your cloth until the bleeding is congealed, and raise the place of cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be restrained as it should be; and what is better and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenchant by .ij. parts, but let the trenches be well spaced to keep longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thick, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have between the two knives one and a half inches wide, and then when you have marked with the two points, and you put the red hot iron above as long as it comes up to the bone, and cut the vein in two points; and be distanced between the two shoulders because it is not joined together by this cautery at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are descending through the veins that are on the test of the head of fury, and it does not benefit any medicine if it is done, and you see the face of the patient twisting, and feels or front walking as if from shivering; and where the oil is wet and so much that the hair of the papers falls out, and the papers are chapped, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it the old "contused cure," and you make to the patient who has this malady the hairs that he has or front, then he makes iii incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as ii should be all over the forehead down until the neck, and the other ii. in ii. ribs above the cheekbones; and guard yourself from the incision of the arteries that are the two ribs above the cheekbones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of iii. thumbs across joined;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then put the spatula sharp from ii parts as here is the shape;
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is below the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the skin which is between the two incisions to all the fat that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision until the other second, and then extract far this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put it in the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the sharp edge toward the flesh near the heart, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the middle fissure. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous up to where it opens into the heart, and then on the other side make another incision in the middle fissure up to the other end; and then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the blood drawn; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths soaked in wine and oil and balsam, and keep that an abscess does not come there; and on the third day untie the bandage, and then administer great amounts of warm water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures for which one heals wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come catarrh acute accustomed, and you see the eyes closed and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in perform a sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come from many veins, and the mother cure that is, this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a great cut between the eyebrows, and another of width. And begin from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be until the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the meal; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then apply between the two lips of the fissure cotton old, and linen bandage; then bind above cloths softened in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, that make cartilage.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to prevent cartilage growth entirely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of stopping up ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or similar thing as iron; or seed, as lentils, beans, peas; or flowing thing as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something falls into the ear, like a stone or any other manner of thing that does not join with the ear nor grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, instill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and have him sneeze by means of condiments, and stop his nostrils when sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. Many times it comes out through this cure; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with very fine tweezers, which is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, it is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine single-edged needle; and if it does not come out by this, make a bird's beak of iron and thrust the head of the beak or hole into the ear very forcibly, and stop what is around the beak with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the beak; then try to force it out, because many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take glue of what birds use for their nests, and put it on any instrument which is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and try to force it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not follow all these things that we have said, then you haste to split the ear so that an abscess may come, and spasm; and the manner of splitting is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and making a small split at the root of the ear in the fat or where it depends; and let the split be like a crescent moon, as far as you come to the bone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it carefully with your mouth; and care for it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer one spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer incision to that grain. But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist for the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine tweezers and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ear water therefore that falls on the patient must use of externalities of condiments first, and ample the ear of old cotton. And let him be lying upon that same ear where the water is. If it goes out by this, it is good. If this not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; and put them in the patient one pierced of his ear, and let him lie on it from his feet another side, and firm one stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease of doing this of stone in stone until the water goes all out, and thus if it goes all out. And if you see, then take one rush, and put one end in the ear, and the other chief hold in the fire until the most soft rush be burned; then make another part of other rushes until the water goes all, as we have said in the stone.
