En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body which one can feel, then administer the extraction of pincers; and this is the thing more light to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not profit, then it behooves that you look at the ear in the sun: if there appears any worms, then treat them with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, then take the canine of which here is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed forming to all the caine; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey to come out, then stop around the caine of cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, because of this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or of iron, narrow below to one small holes, and above open to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation one instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; then throw your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the caine, and let the caine be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be one pock heated over the fire thus when you distill them in the ear; and keep that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the Stoppings of Ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by the swelling of wounds, or by flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come from within the ear so one cannot see them; and sometimes they have i.e. a point of pus from the hole, and it is seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes from within so that it cannot be seen, is of great healing in more positions, and for this reason you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all this spatula from this.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it aged and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh growing or bone of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, as long as that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the suppuration is in the ear, take one razor subtle and light and heat it a little at the fire, then put it into the ear's flesh. If you feel the suppuration that the patient feels great pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw out the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ointment that comes on papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, so it is necessary that you stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and the root with a spatula; then put on its place powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorticate, so cauterize with the lenticular subtle cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is worth mutes; and many times they return, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	of the gristle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come on paper the eyes things that seem gravel in its shape and in its hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a gathering of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the work is such: take ward if the hail moves from one side and another, and this is a light thing to know; then make the large opening, then the skin lightly on each side, then take with tweezers, and the cut. If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the paper, then it grieves nothing to the patient; and if the fissure is great, so assemble with a stitch, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the ointment restores it quickly and heals flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending in the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper, and holding the hail with tweezers, cut it and press on both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the hail is cut, leave the eye of salt water, and cure the place with that which heals flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is made in the webs of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and grieves much to their eyes, and they come to them the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces afterwards, and sleep on, and are their papers under their eyebrows moist that the flower and appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye. And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinarnach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your palm; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinarnach from each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinarnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula a trenching a slit of a width, and let it not be more than the wound that one makes to the vein; and make the skin apart as far as you come to the exinarnach; and in more dispositions comes exinarnach from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then a whole piece of cloth charpit between your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left as much as it is spread; and keep that you do not add into the slit, until you come to all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind him.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the opening does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then gently widen the fissure until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place on the site, and restrain with bands.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it has such men who grind herbs and place them on top to corrupt the moisture that is present. Then treat it until it is healed. And if an abscess comes to the site, then treat it with soothing ointments until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on paper there grow hairs other than the natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and bring about many diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the eyelids and albuginea, so much that it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to .iiij. manners: either by cautery in all fire, or by medicine aqua according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and is done either by incision and stitching or by cauteries, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, put an awl with .i. thread above; and be it below the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow beside these hairs, and pull .i. thread upwards to all the paper, and turn it back to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, to all the spatula copying, from the large tear to the small one; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then place on top of the paper a figure of an enclosure, as the myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if at this which needs it one cuts a large quantity of the paper according to that the paper is softened; then make to all the spatula above the .ij. lines that you have marked, and begin from the larger tear to the small one; and be it one of the slits near the natural hairs in the width of a root, then put the awl in one of the .ij. angles of the heart, then scrape it all; then assemble the .ij. lips with a suture of an awl with .i. thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air to the superfluity of the threads on the .ij. eyebrows to nothing sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, take no care of it, then leave the suture and the threads up to .iij. days or .iiij.; then cure the wound without suturing with dry and constricting things, because the paper comes back alive at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is moved (as they say the ancients), and this work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if in another manner: and is that you draw on the paper a figure which is as much like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, at three inches wide according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which surmounts the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle which has one thread, and put it within the figure; and put one other thread along the large tear, and the second thread along the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin over what you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing on one and on the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make .ij.  caines by art, and .ij.  subtile liens as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on that which rises above the paper of the eye, and strain the .ij. caines of the .ij. parts forming; and let it remain thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and shrink and draw together, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, if you cut it again with more force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn together, and if the paper has been lifted, and the hairs will prick no more; and this is the form of the .ij. caines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works is such that you take a fine needle, and put into it 1 thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and tie one and the other finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another thread of silk very thin, and tie the chief of the threads; then put the patient’s head on your own; and be facing the sun so that the work is clarified, because it is a subtle and fine work; then put the needle to all the chase in the root of the hair adjusted, and let it pierce into the paper hastily until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put into the chase that hair, if there is 1 or 2 or 3 or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come forth to all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes forth from the hole above and that you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows on it; and if the hairs are small, accompany it with 1 long hair of the natural ones, and be raised with that one or you leave it, as long as it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease that is called “aleacrati” or rot comes in the eye, if there are .ij. manners: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens by suddenly of wound, or cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of the work in it is that you split that suture, and loosen the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not fitting that you use in the cure of it things that dry and constrict. For if you do those things, then the illness returns worse than the first; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or althea and linseed seed be cooked, and aqua dijon melted into any of the oils, and envelop a tent, and cure it from that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form that it was before; and these works that we have said are nothing but addresses of this illness, that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This illness which is called "axacrati" truly is dislocation; and it is natural and accidental.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should, it is good; if not, then take one razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make .ij. fissures or cuts inside the paper; and let the heads of the .ij. fissures be the .ij. angles of the incision that you have cut, and make ones angles so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no "j griech"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its cost is raised below, from those who follow the paper, then join the .ij. separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure it with what we have said of softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the skin, and according to what is above; then bind between the two leaves of a tent, as I said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, because it is very diverse in form, and the sages masters equip everything with all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what it is necessary for work and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the skin's surface
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to a man's eye in such a manner that the skin above is glued with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the skin, and raise it up; and while holding the tweezers, as long as you cut what is attached to the spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient does not suffer that the spatula too sharp nor bleaches the eye; and let your incision, by which you peel back this assembly, be slight, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and all this assembly is healed, and one never uses salt water in the eye, but rather sweet water, and honey; then put between the skin and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened with oil; and after the third day use the honey and things inward until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two ways: it is nervous and similar to one hard silk, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to white frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and cured burns like pinches, it cannot be; and one and the other semblance begins towards the large tear, and crosses little by little until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and raise the paper with your hand, then coil the angle with a small doubleure, and lift it upwards; then take a needle, and put in it one hair of horse, or goat, or ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the angle, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and lift it upwards, and scrape all around the edge of the angle that follows the prunele and silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear with all the spatula subtle and as small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear, so that through the incision the body of tears does not come as is accustomed; and no times lift the angle only once, and with the thread, as we have said; then scrape it all around the spatula like this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a little bit of crushed silk, and with the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it of what it needs until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved, and you cannot put the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lighter little sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason is quick, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red collar and crushed silk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess pouch, then milk it and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh near the tear duct bothers the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it with a thread, and cut away a portion but not too much that the flow of tears doesn't come; then distill in the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men are born at times with red flesh, and it covers the iris and restricts the pupil, turning them outward, resembling a rose of balance; and the work is that the patient puts their head in your hands, then opens their eyes, and coil all that flesh with thread suitable to those eyes, and support it with force; then cut the first piece of flesh, and go on cutting all the way down to the end, and be careful that you do not touch the white part of the eye during this work;  and let the incision be like the spatula which we have mentioned in the incision of the angle, and small forces from which one removes the pupil as this chapter later demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of silkworm crushed or distill red mercury and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the oil cotton with a little yolk, so that it be assured of hot abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the skin closes over, and you doubt hot abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with things soothing hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as long as flesh is attached in the eye by this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, it is necessary that you heal the cure of each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works as long as you see that this limb suffers that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Red veins that are covered over the eye and take away its work and weaken the eye every day. It is therefore important that you look first at the eye, whether it's good or bad, and there is no other illness except for the red vein; therefore, in this manner: instruct the patient to put their head on your lap, then suspend those veins all over the body according to his wisdom, and let the incisions be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two incisions be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then with this coil you force those veins subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after another, until you see removing those veins outside of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, if you distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrode what remains of the red vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to collect all these in that hour, so make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and let it for some days until the pains are appeased and be assured of hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before as long as it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and medicine burning according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it should die, and treat all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, then the ruler has all the tools of this form; and it is called "sharp head," and be made from fire iron to one chief rounded, and be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on top the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little bit as long as you know that the corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place of drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is soldered and it is growing flesh, and the body of the bow is soldered, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew and is not an abscess, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, then there is no other remedy but to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take one forest according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the shaft be tapered until the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then put it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand from the eye  i. poc, then turn to all the forest until it pierces the bone and feels the patient by what comes in this if he holds his hand on his nose; and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens the places, so goes the matter to the nose; so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open and there is no disturbance to the nose or lessening, then it behooves you to bind the patient; then heal, then put on suction cups or a haeretel without injuring to suck, then put on the eye  i. linen made of acaice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye, and emplaster above with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths enough soft, and double each in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye has need; then bind it from above with a hard bandage, and restart the suction cups to suck without injuring; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, then it behooves you to strain it much; then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good; if not; then restart the emplastering and cloths and linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the dislocation of a linen cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear comes in the woven cloth, then open it and there come forth like i. grain of resins, and is expectable to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put one needle in the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is i. double thread of the part of the seam; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then withdraw the needle and put the other half linen oil in abundance of an egg; and let it stay until the thread falls with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at no time the wound is restrained by the grape each part of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce it with a fine spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter immediately; then withdraw it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bowel of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This sickness which is called “alcunnati”  is nothing but a bowel which is assembled in the eye, seeming like a thorn descending, and it is not a thorn; and the manner of the appearance of the work so is that you make the sick person sit on i. seat prepared and straight, then take the chief between your hands of ii. parts, and move it as much as you see the bowel coming up to your eyes; then be ens fichie, and do not descend and be discombree the light, and let the sick person see things as he would; and if it does not descend below, know that it is a thorn, and if the descending of the bowel is not appeased as we have said. So make the sick person sit between your hands, then take the spatula subtle and make on the corneal tissue i. poc by the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal tissue and the crown, as much as the bowel issues; and when it is issued, so distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then be cured of other cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of thorns of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have done the appearances of needles in division, and those that it is fitting for to perceive; so in work according to health. It is fitting that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and bind their healthy eye and restrain it very strongly; then place the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument which is called "almagda," or with your left hand, if the eyes are right; then put the point of the instrument beside the crown by the width of a thread in that white part of the eye at the side of the less tear, then thrust the instrument which is called "almagda" virtuously, and restrain your hand until it pierces in the white part of the eye, and feel that "almagda" comes to the empty thing; and it is fitting that the measure of the way "almagda" is to the perfect measure of the space that is from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument up to where the needle is, then express it down one way after another. If the needle now goes down, if the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After repose, i. little, and if the eye goes up the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ens fichie and it does not go up, take "almagda" lightly by turning your hand poc and poc; and then put back in the eye a poc of silk gemme, and leave of ceu the eye inside. Then put on the outside of the eye a stopper or linen soaked in rose oil and abun d'uef, and tie with the healthy eye. Now, and those who are of our time, we put on top as comin broiet with abun d'uef.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if "almagda" cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it is fitting that you take the instrument which is called "alberit," of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deep in it, but make one subtle, then put almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with one pillow, so that he sleeps on his back in one dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in this same dark house, and prove his sight, and let him see some things, and then put him back on the band until the seventh day; and it is not proper that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you align this because the liquid mounts hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And when the abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who soothe the abscess; and when it is calmed, then untie the sight and put on his face one orilliet to cover any day, and be in that dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and turn back to his affairs; and know that none of the disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almagda pierce, so that one sucks the liquid, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of the almond, for those who do not know them they see them; and be of rain properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of the wing of this same subtlety, and the last one in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh out from the vein
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At no time are veins born or joined together diversely, so there are none that seem like scorpions with many legs; and if there are such ones where there is flesh scarred of a bad color, and if there is flesh soft of good color. In that one then of these veins which is soft, and not scarred, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands against the sun; and open his nostrils, and throw the ointment onto those veins, and remove them outwards; then cut what you can sustain with the sharp spatula of one part, until you know that this flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, open it entirely i.e., with instruments subtle and light, so that nothing remains; and if there is no swelling or abscess, cover it as it is proper; and if it is a malignant abscess, haste and cauterize it until the blood is extinguished and all the pus is removed, then apply either boiling water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the nose works, and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is clean; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so the instruments cannot come to cut; therefore you must put i. a thread of linen about a finger thick, and be knotted at both ends, and have between each knot a space i. a finger or less; and put the patient's head of the thread into his nostril at its bottom, and draw it gently until it comes out through the nostril inside the mouth; and many times do children in school this way, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it; then hold the head coming from the nostril with one hand, and the other head coming from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart while keeping them which are or thread. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then draw the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before; do this iii. days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything that is left of flesh; and then put on the nostril a poultice of flax for several days until it is clean, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, with which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a can, and you lead it thus; and if you wish, make a closed can, and let the instruments be full to cleanse the head; and have i. handle at the top for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the beginning of birth a sickness arises which is called "telul," and it grows and becomes large very quickly, to the point that it is a thing to behold; and for this reason it behooves you to cut it at the beginning, and pull out all the pus, then put on its place the cautery or medicine burning; and if one delays to cut it until it is large, beware, if it is hard, of dark color, with poor sensation; do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts it once, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be all cut out, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the birth is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these works cartillages, it profits little because in some men. It is therefore necessary if this happens to any, see if the wound is fresh to all its blood; and then adjust the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it is healthy; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then assemble the two lips to a suture, and restrain them, and powder over powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of ointment of strong or other soothing ointment, and leave it until it falls by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have let you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's hands happen inside the lips abscesses hard, seeming to grains of vezis, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut on each knot, and take it with tweezers and cut it in every part; then apply there after incision of vitriol ground, until the blood is stanched; and then the leaf of aisil, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh is born on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and leave the wound open for the blood to flow; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other restraining and drying powders; and if this flesh returns after the incision, and often happens so, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and pull out the teeth or scabs appear, until nothing remains; and thus do of blackness and greenishness, and jaundice and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it's good; if those no, so it begins again the second day and the third, until you have all pulled out; and know that teeth need diverse forms of instruments to pull out, according to what the work shows you, because the scraper with which one pulls out outside the teeth have other forms than those with which one pulls between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait to draw as much as you can, because one must not do it hastily; for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to remove.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth aching. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and thinks that it is a saintly tooth, and draws out the good tooth; and nevertheless the pain does not depart from him for this reason, as long as the evil remains, because we have already seen this happen to our own kin; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a strong spatula in order to ward off the gums from all parts; then move it with your fingers or with tweezers at the first place and place, as long as it is well loosened, then firmly attach the tweezers; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After you have extracted the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and push it gently into each part, and move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with a poultice in the place where it is pierced; and restrain it subtly with tweezers so that it does not break when you pull it; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum in order to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take good care that you do not break it and leave a part behind, and return to the patient through the malice of the root greater pains than the first. And beware that you do not do as ignorant healers do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and bring nothing of what we have recounted; but they often bring great disease through the incision of this, for the roots that remain, or because of the jawbone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or water and salt; and if there comes a discharge of blood, which often happens, apply to the place vitriol ground; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to what one moves the teeth first, be long points and big handles, that they do not double when you will draw the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be big members so that they do not bend when drawing, and be of well-made iron, and be toothed for better holding.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains in the drawing, so it is fitting that you put on the place cotton moistened in butter i. day or ii., until the wound be softened, then put the pliers which are called 'algefri', because of this the head seems beak of care; and be inside made also as a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a spatula, because of this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root leaps out with those, it is good; if those do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the shape of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
