Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it may not break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not numbered; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one breaks not the bone of the horse or of other bones, as it can, then he seeks the instruments that are necessary, that I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove; and then return to its place of medicines suitable for those, and if it has in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it befits that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or trim it; therefore the edge; and if it is near with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be of pointed iron at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping a little bit each day for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, so the file of a certain form as this is:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file of which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little each day lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks; then the plain at the end to nothing a scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pierces the tongue, so it is necessary to file the sharpness so that it is equal, so that it does not pierce the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front loosens, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press upon it so that it moves without pain, and you have cured it with constricting medicines, and this is not good; if this is the case, it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and putrefies, but the gold does not change; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, but according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth misaligned, take the thread and bring it double between the two sound teeth, then put the wires between the bad teeth, if there are one or more, until you come skillfully to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering up to the place where you began, and strain your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, and bring them together, and place them between the sound tooth, and put it in such a way that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it unties, or the thread breaks, then restrain it with another thread; let it remain and serve in this way until its end, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two sound teeth, and the two bad teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, fresh against fresh, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and patient should intervene, and sometimes the form of a tooth made from bone of walrus is made, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is restrained as we have said, and remains and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue or nature; which is born thus; or by accident of a sutured wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is stiffness or knotting, and this is from the suture of a wound, so put the awl and cut the wide ligament; and guard that the cutting is not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done, raise the head with warm water and honey, or cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen; and apply the ointment to the sick person every night, so that the ligaments cannot suture. And if bleeding comes, put vitriol ground on the place; and if the bleeding does not stop, cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with other cures until it is healed
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a fiery color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, put the awl and make it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding persists in your work, put vitriol ground on it until it is extinguished, then return to your work until you draw all out; then raise the head with honey and salt, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	At times there come within the throat bubbles which are called «godath», and these are properly called the .ij. almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take heed: if it is abscesses hard of small sense and of fusse color, do not touch them with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the decrease of blood; but let it until it is dead, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color, return, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first look if the abscess warms rests and is appeased. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his arms be in your health, and open the mouth and take the serjans between his hands, and press the tongue below all the instrument, from which is the form; and be it of silver or of iron subtle as one knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, so take the oncine and stick it in the almond, and draw it forcefully upwards as much as you can; and do nothing of the fabrics with it, then cut with the instrument, from which is the form, that seems like forces; but anyway the chief are bent, and one place to the other, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or d'andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut with pliers, from which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenching on one side and the other side name; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and thus, and if decorrement of blood happens, so gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then cure it until it is healed; and some times other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them as you did the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I medicated a woman of an abscess that was born inside her throat, that is to say one abscess of small sense; and I had well closed the whole throat, so that the woman could not expire by the passage which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus one day or two. And the abscess was so mounted that it had been put two rains by the two openings of birth. I therefore immediately, and tied in one one incision, then pulled out the thread, and with a great portion of bow; then refit another piece in the other opening of birth, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after which I inserted the incision into the abscesses, and cut a part, and only a little bit of blood came out; and thus was the throat passage of the woman unblocked, and she began now to drink water, and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I engaged it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus he remained without growing; and I left those parts, and do not know what God did to her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the uvula is swollen and long, it is called “perpendicular”; and if it is somewhat large and rounded, it is called “uvula”. When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess of the tonsil is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary for you to cut it; and the one that is rounded, assembled, and not long; and it is sanguine or reddish-colored or black, then it is necessary for you to make a shallow incision in it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument about which we have made remembrance before; then insert the needle into the uvula, and pull it downwards, and cut it at .i. out of .ij. instruments that I have said in the incision of the .ij. almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves the voice, and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the .ij. almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear to be cut, then it is necessary that you use an instrument to cauterize the feeling of fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp and thin. And it is that the patient put his head in your bosom, and then press his tongue with the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confine with a very hot iron, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and by employing the end of this instrument, because of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on his head a hair or one puts the medicine, as the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the uvula; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles come from his mouth of the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the palate; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the uvula, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it burn and the incisions of the medicine be appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton adheres on the uvula; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and fall after .iiij. days or .v.. And if you have need to begin the cauterization of the medicine again, then begin it again, and after the cauterization, wipe around the uvula, with cotton dipped in butter, and purify what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in 1 pot, and put it inside, and boil it; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have 1 instrument of hair according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or iron, and let the one of the heads be put in the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises to the uvula by the caine, until the uvula is mortified; after which it begins again, until the uvula dries out, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not make this except at the decline of the hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a caine and put inside its head a strip of egg, so that the mouth of the sick person does not get too hot; because the strip of egg does not let the vapor heavily burden the mouth, and it is a good cure altogether safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish, or any thing, gets stuck in the throat; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it behoove you to make the sick person vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it will expel the thing through vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or 1 mouthful of dry bread; and tie to the sponge 1 thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will get stuck, and then you draw it out further; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take 1 instrument of plank according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of life come to it, nor push in the bone; and move it better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows whether it is well or the thing is difficult; so he pushes down, or pulls it up with all the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the throat's bleeding
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No remedy for bleeding in the throat is given by medicine, as I said in the division; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient in the sun, after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you about. And if you see the bleeding, treat it with all .i. small awl, or fine forceps suitable for this purpose. And if this is not enough, take a well-groomed dog hair, and put it into the throat of the patient, then push in the end of the dog hair .i. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient is feverish all day. Then take a full .i. goblet of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the bleeding feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument that I have described in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times because it will come down without suffering. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take i pot or there are hot coals, and let the bottom be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that one put the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane into his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the sinus; and the sinus will now fall, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then the necessity is that it should be released by this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument that is used to treat the sinus is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers so that they can enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has sharpness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many resemblances of abscesses are, according to what the memory comes after here from one and the other in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in .ij. manners which one is in its same semblance, and of those that it holds moisture. And the second manner so is for the places where they are on the body. Because the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if to abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the bow is mature according to its accomplishment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are crusted, and do not die according to their accomplishment, such as abscesses which are near joints. Because when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it as long as it is putridly inflamed, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which reason it is a cause of contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the foundation, so pierce it then as long as it is mature; and it does not become that you pierce an abscess crusted without accomplished digestion, except that which is near the foundation, that it may not be putrid, and be elongated inside, and a fistula comes; and cannot heal in a great term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to its accomplishment, and it is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and of the redness, and of the swelling and of the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more dependent the place of the abscess, and where it appears to open; and be the perforation of the long one of the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or on the feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pliability.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In these which are suppurating, according to the member. And when an abscess is in its place filled with flesh, it is worth knowing that you let the perforation until it is confirmed in digestion accomplished, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, it will lengthen the body of the venom from it, and it is full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of it. And if any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member has need. And it behooves that you bring in small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the semblance of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it behoves to cover the heart, and cover; when it is become as one drapery, and is deadened, then it behooves to do as is done to buboes: and if there are such that are cut in three angles, and if there are such that one covers as the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the angres; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and semblance cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no chief, as superficial abscesses, it behooves that you pierce them completely; and it behoves when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then plug the abscess until the next day, then do not draw out anything directly; do this many times from great to great, until all the pus is gone; likewise if the patient is of feeble virtue, or pregnant woman, or small children, or old men decrepit. For the spirit trembles at any time with the issue of the pus, that by chance the patient dies, and you do not take it amiss.  Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat incision, then bring in tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, then it behooves that you put in each one a tent so that it comes one against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have covered it around, then it behoves that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen rags without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then untie, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold water and ice, and wet one drape, and put it on the place where blood is flowing many times. And if the bleeding persists, then bring governance and cure, and the powders that I have said in hands the places in this book, and if it is in winter's time, and the place or the abscess is much nervous, then it behooves that you put on tents and drapes moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it behoves that you put on drapes moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as behooves, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is important to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of  the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of the sores on the head that come in small abscesses, and are ways of ours that are in cloth, like the joiner's of a linen, and many are similar. There are some fatty ones, and such that have moisture as well as poultices; and there are those that are hard and stony at the cutting, and there is no doubt that if the artery does not work against it. And the works of the waist so is that you experience to all i. instrument which is called "entromissoire", because its form comes later, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then you let it out from above the long one. And when the moisture is emptied, it peels off without leaving anything behind the hair that contains that moisture, for it returns to where it was when we leave nothing; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and cover those who are left over from the night. And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that there is nothing left from the night; then cure the wound with ointment as seems fitting, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds i. fat, then cut it according to this form, of the long one; and lay your tweezers, and peel it from all sides, and put all your care into extracting the cot from where it lies; and if the artery works against you, do what I have told you later. And so do with the abscess if it is stony, and of the cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the boil on the pus-filled abscess and moist, it is lighter, because there are a few bloods. And if in some of these abscesses or chief where it has no moisture, and of these were i. abscesses that I copied or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as well as a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break; and if one had made any of it, one would have done as well to wound as with a stone. In other abscesses coming or chief, were those that come to the chief of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should be always at the lowest point, so that they may flow out the pus; and cure as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come from other parts or bodies, and are numerous, and are intertwined with each other. And each scrofulous is properly within its own coat, as well as the pustule of the chief, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrophules are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are some malignant that do not want to obey to health. In those therefore that you see of good disposition at the touch, and is similar to the color of the body, and mute from each part and is not painful to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; then it is proper that you cut it from above, and remove the skin from each part, and the two lips of the heart as one piece, if you need them, as we have said in pustules of the chief; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and do not make the spathulum too large nor trenching, so that the hands slip, and do not look too far forward, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, as long as you accomplish it; then with your index finger see if there remain any small pustules, so cut them and clean them. And if in the root of the pustule there is a large vein, it does not befit you that you cut that pustule at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it hang by it, without annoyance; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole pustule, it befits that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then as long as there remains no superfluity for the size of the pustule. It befits that you attend to cutting the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said. Those pustules that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears more; and pierce it thus as the one before stated, in dependence, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment causing flesh to grow, until it is healed.
de squinance	of a hernia
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinance, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help them, because all the veins and the arteries of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two cheeks.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three or four circles, a small slit across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those they are comparable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to the whole opening, then split the skin as much as it comes to the windpipe; and escape the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe that flows out through the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew them together alone against the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one does not do this until the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect comes from the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, one cuts open the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And therefore they commanded to sew up the wound and care for it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took  a knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called by her to heal her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and so well that it had not cut a vein nor led further than the throat, and the wind was blowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and closed the wound, and treated it until it healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it came to pass for the young woman that she was red of voice, and returned after to her disposition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for which reason I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "goiter," and it is a large abscess in the color of a bruise, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; the natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which is similar to fat in us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and he has fear, and it does not become to work to make outside than in this which is small, and the proof and seeks to all the introducer
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it also as our fat, and cannot at any vein, if the cut, as we cut ours, and the train to its whole crest, if there is any of it;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and surround well soon, and the cure as it befits, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are to us, of which I will say all the likenesses.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And or it is fitting that I say all the difference that is between ours and out.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that out is sometimes and fever holding, as long as the boil is not passed, and is accomplished the putrefaction; therefore rests the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the ours has no heat nor fever nor pain, and contains .i. cyst, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a blister, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two resemblances, whether dry or moist, and very colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the wound, that you examine and inquire first of all about the instrument called "entromissoire," according to what its form will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses of the wound is that you prick or moisten the place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then that it be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the entromissoire, and take care in those that jump forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, what color it has, do as I have said of other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introducer there comes moisture, know that it is fatty, so do it in a cross and take it with forceps, and slightly scarify each side and guard the coat where it lies so that you draw it healthy with the needle.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it healthy, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it stays for a little while, and the wound does not grieve, then apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and hold the wound closed, and put above it soothing things, a hot poultice, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, then sew the two lips of the wound together, and cure it with those who generate flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is contrary or otherwise if you are in haste and apply the place of ground vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound is rotting, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to cover those that remain from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the introits instruments, and they are in .iij. manners: great and medium and small; and there are .iij. squares which are called «albaret», and .i. that is called «breb», and there are in .iij. manners: great, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and they are more proven black plumb for surrounding the curves of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are in .iij. manners: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the hooks are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks which have two curves in three ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And there are hooks which have three curves, and are also in three ways; and there are hooks which have two curves, and hooks of a single curve only, and are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these for what they do is cutting, and there are some that do not cut except from one side, with which we scrape the veins, because one does not cut the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these instruments are the probes put into handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and there are of three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one should not use it except in their fleshy parts, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and groin, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and at no time is made one other instrument small, resembling the skin of fists, according to this form, for which one draws blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at no time in the place that is healthy for opening of veins and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	No times swollen the breasts of some men when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should be according to this form of these lines up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound, stopping bleeding, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitching, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast leans down and is softened because of its size as women have, then make two cuts above the ribs, with two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	Of which one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said of stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, for that the patient does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it there until it softens the remaining and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous nodules in which there is pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those then that contain pus should be cut according to this form, from the line b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole core that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound some old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as before to it until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like the appearance of scrofulous sores, then make it as we have said in cutting open scrofulous sores, and if the wound enters inward, administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the artery rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn shut, abscesses often occur, and this also happens with an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if the expert knows that it is due to the artery, then they should make the abscess longer by cutting.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at your hands, that is to say, tightening; and when it is for the vein, it is reopening appears
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the arms and on the neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It therefore behooves to avoid the cure of iron, and the one who is at the head also behoove to avoid, and in the one who is swollen from artery that goes through the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the opening of the stones, and separate beautifully the artery from the cloths, as long as it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then put beneath it a needle, and make it pierce until the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in 2 lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the 2 arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point the place which is between the 2 links of an intromitter as long as the pus issues from it, and let the abscess be discharged.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the cure that engenders a boil, as long as the link hangs.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure those which are anointed coming to these, as long as it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is at the size of the vein, then you must hold with your hand that which you can of the abscess to all the skin
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then push the needle under where you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be i.i. double thread, so that you draw it to the other side
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or bind it from one of the two parts to the two ends of thread
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the threads are not firm enough, then insert another needle into all i. thread under the whole abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four loops
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the superfluities issue from it, then cut the superfluity of the heart and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place one cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer treatment of tents and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come in the nerves when they are  worn out, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all the places where there are joints, and it is i.e., grief abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and it is in many positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one holds it firmly, the patient feels pain, and is not at all part of the body, but below the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down or up, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear that there would be a contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one who is at the top or on the forehead, makes the skin like a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers, and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it with the scalpel, and flay it, then scrape it, and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Never happen in the belly and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called “fungus” because of the resemblance to it, and is the root subtle, and the head large; and there are small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two stomachs that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and they had small roots, and they were slightly split, and some moisture came out of them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 ounces, and the work in the incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if he cuts with a spatula wide, and be in your presence the cautery to fire. For at the cutting comes many times too great decorremens of blood, and if the without you vaint, so then hasten to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one thread of lead well made, and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	And then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the lead thread until it heals the joint, and heal by itself without work; and if the roots are large, fear to cut even together for the belly, but you may well cut half
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it that it not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the tendon which is of dark color and poor feeling and with milk-like appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess festering, and I will come to the cure of syphilis later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the skull is moved
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the skull comes from a cautery wound or fissure of the sfiafac, and is on the belly and has no bones, as it happens in other wounds, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the sfiafac and the exit of the bone, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is because of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with his hands, it returns up, and then comes back down, and perhaps it is closed, and grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and for strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is puffed up when touched, and the work is that you look if its appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then it is necessary that you leave the treatment. Because there is doubt and fear about it, as I have told you in this chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
