Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the belly, then you must command the patient to hold his arm, and be outstretched straight, then place a hand all around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to breathe deeply between your hands;
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula;
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then extend the half of the abscess upwards to the whole great incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind it with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the wound be clean.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open half of the abscess extending on the linen, and put your index finger into it, and explore its interior.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the linen, untie it, and bring the intestine out to the outside of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find it boiled, take it with the forceps, and cut away the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein opposes you, then go well around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two for threads, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you make appear;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it can rot, and let the dead flesh fall by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then treat it as appropriate, and shave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as appropriate, and close the place;
dou chancre	Of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of ulcers, and how one must work them by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say the ulcer is prevented in the marshlands, and great caution should be exercised in its treatment, and ancient ones said that when an ulcer is in a place where one can shave it like an ulcer which is on the breast, and in the hip, and in similar places, and one must remove it entirely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not proper that you approach it, because I have never been able to heal any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion; then make the patient's good bed to perform the operation; then lay your forceps or ulcer, and shave it on all sides, and take away everything completely without leaving anything behind; and let the blood run out entirely, and gently press the place with your hand or any object, and if the bleeding from the wound goes against the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it as long as the bleeding is extinguished; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is made by medicines, and the one that is cured by iron; thus it is outlined only; and one must not touch with iron in these 2 resemblances: namely, tympanites and hyposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this resemblance of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of belly and similar things; if you do not touch with iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus work:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	lift the patient upright with your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the bottom then take the  spatula spineous according to this form: And be trenchant in 2 parts at the point, and nevertheless, it should not be so deeply that it can come until the intestine when it is put in, and do not let it bleed;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy is established towards the intestines: if it is necessary that you cut above the belly three fingers straight below the nipple; and if the dropsy is from the disease of the liver, then make your cut on the left side of the belly three fingers; and if it is from the spleen, then on the right, and it is not proper for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and bring it out, and raise your hand to the whole spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or less; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to its place eight, and this is the place of the water, then the pull out this instrument because this is the form: And it is similar to a silver needle fine, and it is of iron or archaut light, and in the lower part one small hole; and on one side three holes; and two on the other; and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision with which scribes cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	at the head above is the alemmele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, because if you empty more than it is necessary in that hour, by adventure the patient may die for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls faint, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But in void according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick person signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now for the heart which stops the opening which is on the syfac, because of this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument again another day, if you see the sick person suffering those, and treat of the water a little quantity.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this no day, and guard yourself from following until there remains but a little bit of water. And if you doubt about the sick person, and you let him much water, then cure of the burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and if he stays to drink; and cure of drying medicines as long as he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes a child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. If this is the case, it must be treated as soon as possible with a very fine needle according to this form: then put a very fine plug of lead into the opening, and tie it and keep it there for three or four days. And when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose opening is small, if they are treated with the lead plug as we have said, it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its place are blueish because none are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the penis and the scrotum raised as high as a feather, so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; and guard against bleeding which often comes, and if it happens, let him who stanches blood stanch the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come to this [area] of the penis, and is a loathsome appearance of flesh; and there are malignant ones and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to prick them with .i. one subtle needle, and scrape and clean all of them, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blister is malignant, of putrid color and stench, then it behooves you to bring cautery to it. When you have scraped it, and if the blister is in the bottom of the penis, and has part inside the flesh and part outside, then it behooves you to remove the blister that is inside first; and when it is healed, then cure the outside. For when you cure it altogether, it is not as certain that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its penis and scrotum; so it behooves to cut away all that which is black and corrupt, then put on a plaster of honey and flour that is made from the bark of pomegranates and vetives, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if the hemorrhage occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: The cautery helps in two ways together: that is to say, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must pour or conduct a chain of lead from the penis and piss on the patient among; and when the skin is raw at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scarify it with one instrument, until the tendons are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a grievous thing to discuss these, then it is necessary that you scarify it with one spatula none in the head of the penis and the skin; then sever gently between two, and put one fine linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the separation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will, and properly on children, then it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the most part of the masters and healers who did circumcision around one [inch], and with force, and to all a new knife; so it was good because there are two layers, and by chance if one chops above and remains the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is better to cut and the pain is doubled, and at the purification which is around one inch [of distance from the glans] the point of the member is not guaranteed; and at the purification of the angle by chance the iron escapes, and the work is spoiled, and many times they are born such that they do not need purification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification which is made with forces to the whole line of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, so it cuts equally in one whole tension; but that the thread be well wrapped around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only making him tie the thread around the rod so much, and then make it enjoy in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then make it stay between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and blow or heart, and drive it upwards as long as the head of the rod is inside; then purify it well of the dirt that is assembled in it, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it below one pock at another thread; and hold it as two points by the second league to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the two leagues, then lift the heart upwards gently and drive the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood be cauterized again and again because that is the treatment; and put powder on and on the powder one drape made of a cooked egg white tempered with rose water, mixed with fine rose oil good and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces in the unification thus is this: the two shoulders should be held and be sharp, and the shoulders also as large as the palms equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the unification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the leaus make an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass three days, and what is below the rod is swollen, let it be so until the abscess has calmed, and the scab slightly; then cut it as you can move, and keep away from the part of the rod, it will not hurt him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if one cuts out too much, and it goes above, it will do no harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of urine retention
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The holding back of urine is from a stone in the kidney, or from blood clotted, or from bowel, or from new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the kidney or at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient’s legs as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary for you to administer extraction with every instrument that is called "syringe," of which this is the form: and it should be made of finely crafted light silver, like the feather of a bird; and its handle should be half a palm long, and be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the exit of urine is that you take one double thread, and tie to the head one pock of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on one seat, and raise his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently put the syringe in the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the belly; then put the syringe forward up to the bladder, and feel the patient come until the thing is empty, and this is not done according to this order unless for those that the conduit or where it goes is twisted; then extend the thread to all the wool pock and pock, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it further, and do correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scrapes or blood come in the bladder, or rot is gathered there, and you see it distilled with sharp waters and medicines, so do to all the instrument that is called "clepsedre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and its lips should be such that the medicine does not escape well,  stopping the shaft without addition, so that if it can be drawn out the moisture, and pushed when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you want to put your medicines in the bladder, place the chief of the tube into the moisture, and draw through the tube that is inside; so you will draw the moisture to the tube, and then firmly reinsert the tube back inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is of silver or of brass, and the head is higher; and under to one breast or where the shoulder joint falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you want to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed by a double thread, and heat one fistful of that moisture over the fire; then put the head of the enema into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder throughout the entire administration of the moisture, until the patient feels that the moisture has arrived at the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly all around; then put one strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a bowl, and put inside that which you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, by pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as reins, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a size; and in the bladder, and in the member; and I will tell it to you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and it appears harene, and grieves the patient his member, and he can many times, and then urinates; and with much of these jumps the foundations; and it is light the healing of the children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old people, and it is as the middle to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter of those who have the large stone, than of those who have the small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is convenient first to purify the patient by clyster, in order to draw out all the mucus which is in the intestines. For it encumbers sometimes to search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and dislocate and move them down so that the bladder descends to the front of the pubis, and it comes out from its high place. Then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is all declining downward; then the queue and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the bladder in the space, then hurry now to cut above the bladder. And if it does not fall at the touch of all, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it into its foundation, and feel the bladder, and when you feel it with your finger, push it towards the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your finger, and put it outwards where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the scrotum upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the scrotum in the part where the incision is made; then put the spatula cutting, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And place between that which is between the hips and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight upon the stone, and the two sides should be either equal or foundation, and let the waist be like a traverse so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if the two sides which are either foundation, that it jumps forth without work; and know that there is such a stone which has angles, and margins: so it is hard to insert; and if it is such as is below, seeming like a gland, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that one therefore where it has angles and margins, make the waist larger; and if it does not jump, then you must extract it with tongs which are like a file at the chief, in order to constrain the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below the one instrument subtle curved at the chief; and if you cannot engineer it thus, then enlarge one pock the opening, and if it is without decortication, then strain it with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	and if there is more than one stone, first put the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull the larger, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, it should be softened, and make a larger wound. Because two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through where the bladder cannot close; but nonetheless try to drain it, or to break it with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, apply to the wound incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top one bandage moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then support the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, thoroughly wash the area with oil and water, then treat it with diaphicon ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and clotting of blood in the bladder, and because of this retained urine, which is known in such a manner that without leap with the urine: therefore put them all in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound of water and ease and soil, and help him in all the ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you tie his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is or conducted by the shaft, and fixed therein, and the urine cannot pass; so cure him of what I say thus, that you cut it many times, and one excuses the cutting by this cure. I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron forest according to this form and be it at three angles fitted into one twig:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the forest in the shaft lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand in the stone poke and poke, until you can feel the stone from the other side; so will come soon the urine, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. Then is it broken, and jumps out with the urine, and is healed the patient;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then make the shaft straight against the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the clotted blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens sometimes that a stone is in women, and if it happens at any time, the cure is grievous, and is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-knowing who reveals herself to the eyes, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more deeply set than the stone of the man, for which reason it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you take a midwife well-knowing, and try to find one. And if you cannot find one, then take no less than one chaste woman who is subtle; and present her with a sage woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her about the incision of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look well if the woman is a virgin: therefore she must press her bottom or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it under her buttock, and recommend to her that she presses her buttocks or con the sick person, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it from great to small from the entrance of the bladder down until it comes to the root of the thigh; then place above the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is moved and appears, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her buttocks above the stone or below, and let the waist be at first little.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then press the root in the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as much as the stone can possibly come out, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and which have veins. If you know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the stone is not removed, put ground vitriol on it and hold it there for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone is gone, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones for men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone does not come out, and it is from the artery that was cut, put the powder on the wound and restrain it with strips and bandages, and do not start again those things, and leave the stone and do not touch it at all, in case the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the wounds are healed, then return to your work, as long as the stone is gone.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquatic ramice is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is from the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e. another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have se poc non.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes from the testicles, and is spread that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is or white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, i.e. long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the edges because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the skin itself, then the abscess is ripe with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the edges and the white as we have said, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture,  examine the entire introducer quickly, for its shape is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the repletion of his body; then he lies on his back, on a thing a little high, and puts under him much of cloth;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then he sits on his left side, and commands the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the sides;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then he takes the spatula, and cuts the skin of the sides among them from their long side up to near their armpit, and let your cut be straight dividing the skin of the sides until it reaches the white fat, and the eschar is carefully removed according to his strength;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the abscess full of water with one large opening, and draw out all the water, and then put your dressings, and raise the abscess up; and do not touch the core of the boils, but only the abscess; cut all or by pieces equally the skin around it, that if you do not cut it well carefully, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer should be of your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the abscess; then assemble the two leaves of the core of the boils to one suture, and then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another malady, then it behooves you to tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flowing of blood; then cut the boil at all its suspension, and draw out the ulcer, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the sharp is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; if you cut the other part as you have done the first evenly, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound a linen cloth half-soaked in rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put another piece of linen soaked in wine and oil, and place it over the two cushions, and put double cloths on top, and bind it above all the linen according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use them of wool padding according to this likeness and be assembled by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the shoulders rests on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the armpit; and the other from the top above the two angles, and let the entire restraint be assembled in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this branch of cautery is medicated in place of iron shears, and that you prick one cautery knife subtle, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac containing the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and burn it with this subtle hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And the cut in all ways that you can, as long as you scrape all; and guard that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salutary; and moves guards against blood loss, and movements than the works of shears;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if no thing makes contrary to you, or abscess or running of blood or other thing, so cure that which makes contrary to you, according to what is before said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to await this work because of its horror, so administer perforation, as I told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the significations that we have said that watery root is there,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	so make the patient sit upon a high seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below to all the spatula width, and put the perforation long along the body; and be wide the perforations, so that all the water runs out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the spot, and tie it, and let for running out the remaining of the water, then cure it as long as the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow into the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you pour a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of hydrophics, for its form is before; and widen i. pc the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after .vj. months or as long, and when it is assembled like before, and so will pass the patient his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this nerve fear comes to more dispositions, for which it seems to me better that one leaves it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the genitals; and this is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	That is to say, by excess of sour and sharp humors that are spread to the genitals, or from percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it finds no pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by adventure are some abscesses grievous and painful, and of dark color, and sometimes comes from our artery, or from the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by our artery, then it is known by the disposition of the hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it does not behoove you to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	That one which is made from the swelling of a vein is known by its disposition at the expression of the touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can well make a cut on this likeness, and on the other parts.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut out the core of the onions, then let the leaf be on top, and the trunk further down white, and free the suspender from all parts of the leaf.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the leaf is already sodden with these new onions, then it is necessary that you pull out the leaf, and cut.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is dry in the white part, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you free all of that membrane, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the shaft is or its rear, then it behooves you to cut it entirely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the works are completed, apply the wound to wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed in an envelope resembling i.e., a tunic, with the softening of the testicles,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves badly when he goes;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this malady is as well-prescribed as fearsome as this one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on one elevated seat, then you tie the suspensory of the testicles down to his two legs
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near to the penis, and the masters braid them, and the extend form.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut with the sharp spatula wide through the vessels, until they are uncovered,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert an awl where it has one double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein came from, and tie it straight to the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut the flesh in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then cure the wound as with others where we prevent bowing, so that no vessel leaks that nourishes one of the sides;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For through these there comes no harm, and if to all the vessels comes life, then it is necessary to draw the sides to all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the flesh does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries out and cannot be aided.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this damage is by the section that comes on the shoulder, or the extension above the belly in the part of the angles, so the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	And this rupture is on the shoulder, or from the extension of it, and these 2 manners of many causes: either by percussion, or by jump, or by straining, or by lifting heavy burdens, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is from the extension of the shoulder, are that there are throbbing pains, in long periods, and do not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and is the abscess even up to the forehead, because of which the pus quickly reaches the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the pus, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscess appears diversely, under the skin near, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the body outward from the pus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines with the abscesses, and are held in, and cause great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron there is fear, because it befits to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to push the intestine into its place in the wound, if it can enter.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either bind it on its neck between your hands, and raise the hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the groin long;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the folds of the waist a point according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that the intestines can issue forth;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then skin the area beneath the flesh of the buttocks as much as the white flesh is exposed on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then put your index finger into the following buttocks, where it is between the white flesh which is beneath the skin of the buttock, and between the second flesh;
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And depart that which is behind the buttock, and between the second flesh; then move with your right hand into the heart of the buttocks, and keep the white flesh on top at your left hand, and raise the buttock to all the flesh towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the assistant that he extend the buttock upward, and untie what is behind the joint;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and if he has any point of the intestine wrapped or white in it hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or it has 1 thick thread made of 10 threads, and put it into the rear part of the white hard substance, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are 4 threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then gather them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the white substance, which we have said is below the skin of the buttocks, with a strong binding of 2 parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wrap the hairs of the threads, and tie them together in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except for an abscess that comes.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the linen straight according to the first linen long two fingers of that one, and after these two linens leave the from under the heart of the groin the greatest of a finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the groin, as much as the without correction, and the bow, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then administer wool moistened in oil, and put it in the wounds, and there administer the linen that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is cauterized the white groin that we have said, after the incision, out of fear of a decrease in blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and let the linen be left until it is soaked through with it; and if it delays in falling off, make it rise with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another dressing, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter, I never saw anyone daring to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch that is assembled to the head, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after the cut above or slightly below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cop it in half, and treat the abscess of those who work, as long as the vessels bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture comes in the bowels, as we have said, and opens them; and do not draw any of the intestines out to the anus, and if any are drawn out, it is bad, and repair them immediately.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And nevertheless if it remains too long in this spot, the wound or syphilis will grow, as long as the intestines are drawn out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the extension of the sinew which is at the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflated its parts and open;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure of this is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then cuts the place of the rupture inflated with a breadth according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then pulls out the sinew which is under the skin that has become accustomed, then takes the red lead and puts it on the place appearing of the sinew;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and the press at the forefront of the belly, then sew the two apparent ones of the back above the top of the spine, and sew one and the other
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the top of the spine, and do not cut of the back nor stretch any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the root of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then cure it by the cure of wounds. And when you cut the threads, if the wound is infected and cures the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The back is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the genitals is softened in some men, because the things that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you see, stitch first the superfluity of the softened skin to three or four firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the  treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that treatment is common in our law, and for this reason I would like that I do not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two ways: one of which is that the mires know how to answer when they are asked, and they know the cure; and the other because we often need treatment from some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rams and other animals. I say therefore that treatment is done according to two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
