Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodite is according to 2 manners as men: one if it is that between the 2 genitals appears also as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. And the other manner is in women, and has on the groin as a penis and 2 genitals.  And the cure of the man and of the woman is that you cut the chars attached all, and the cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine leaps through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a growth attached to the natural part, as long as it is too unsightly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. It is necessary that you cut away the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and don't go too deep, so that bleeding doesn't come, then the cure of other cures until it is healed; and to another growth that arises at the mouth of the vulva, and the employment, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for this reason they call it by the ancients "cow disease." If it is necessary that you cut it as we have said the tenting, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	of wandering if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accident by illness that has come to it; or it is by char ajostee, or dou syfac subtil or espés, and is made em parfont in the marris, or in costez, or desoz, or where so ever; and deffent the conceiving, and the childbearing, and by chance the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these si is by the regart of the baile. If the estoupemens is prochiens apparans, if quier a tes dois or au rait. If it is dou syfac subtil, and it is prochiens as .ij. leivres, if haste, and the ront ensi: put tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, and the woman be sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; then estent the .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, and soit overs li estoupemens; then pren laine, and the moille in oile, and the met sus le leu, and gise the woman a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. And if the syfac is dur and espés, if covient that thou lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. If the estoupemens is de char nee, if la sospent a l’oncine and the cope; and aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; then amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; and ensi soit longement, and li amenistre une tente de lin sec; then soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez. And quant en la marris comes char nee, if covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without care, become accustomed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division the likenesses of those, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many manners of abscess come in the anus, such as chancre and pus-filled abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. Thus it behooves me to say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the anus, which is not of abscesses that boil over; and if you want to know the work of iron, then look at whether the abscess is angry at its beginning and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down, and desire to smell the air: then she hastens the child to come out; so you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it is the head coming first, and the second one with it; and when you see these signs, it behooves to gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends on its head, the second one comes with it, and the body is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it sometimes comes on its feet, and comes out from the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes on her belly, or back, and is converted by chance on her neck, and by other bad figures; so it behooves the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes on its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth loudly, and the virtue of her is weak, then she make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the secondine, and cut at its fingernail until the moisture that is inside is gone; and take the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek muslin with sesame oil; then make her drink and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: so now the child will come out. And if the two hands have emerged, then you must gently reset them bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on one seat, and lift her feet up; then turn the seat over on the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when turning it over; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the knife which is before placed, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes on its feet, then it is necessary to push upwards
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth, until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then prick it with one of the tools and extend it back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	It cannot jump to the hips unless commanded to be pulled, and it is extended from its condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then return it little by little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is gently set.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come healed as we have said, then take a piece of alum, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put it on the woman's genital area inside and outside this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then let him sit upright on his heels up to under the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened underneath, let him apply a cloth of myrrh, and put it under, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then let him sit on a stool, then let him sneeze and restrain his mouth and nose, and take hold of his belly gently, because the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then he puts his hands palm to palm.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	Then he is laid on his neck and hangs his feet down, and lies upon a bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bends his hands palm to palm, and then he takes the hands above his belly, and takes away the cushions below, until it is ready down;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, he takes his feet and moves them forcefully, then moves his belly upward, and puts his hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and wet the child's head back and forth; and instruct the woman to apply ointment as long as the child is ill.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child who comes out with a wide hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to devise to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman lie down, and go away.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it cannot go, put it to lie on i.e., bed, and the legs are straightened.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then administer the ointment that I have recounted;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, put her to sit on i.e., a stool, then study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the child according to the natural figure, and make her sneeze, and command her to  be rubbed until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on his neck, and has spread his hands, and his face turned towards the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It behooves the midwife to hold her hand, then turn it gently back and forth, and the elbow lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is straight, she places it on the padded surface of the altar and oil, as we have said, then she commands her to move it back and forth.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, she makes her sit on one seat and commands her to breathe; and the child sneezes.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the backbone
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be cured in this manner for all the backbone, so cut the backbone at your finger, until the moisture is emptied.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can't stand on its face and neck, then cut from the bulge so it is not held back, and let the child die;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman not to take it out at all;
adonques si istra legierement.	therefore if gently pulled
de l’issue des gemelz	from the separation of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if they are named;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know these, that they are multiplied, and are severed by the sifac who divides them, which is attached to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And at times they emerge as naturally as one from under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they emerge harshly, then the cure is as we have said, and let the bailiff be subtle, and quickly and lightly do what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and thus act as it brings salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Never are they formed in the marshes i.e. one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and all are formed into the shape of a child by the measurement of its wise glory
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it behooves the bailiff to know all these things, for by chance similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so it is done according to what is fitting
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure a woman of a dead fetus or womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands.
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue and does not have an accident or she fears death.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is necessary that the woman be supported on her back, and her shoulders inclined downwards, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister sets the comb of two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it does not touch the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mare with moist oils with mucus of altea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the boy's hands with these oils and these mucuses;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then put them gently in the mare, then put one fistful where she puts her hooves that are suitable to those,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take ward if the child is appearing that he descends onto his head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If you put the incisions in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or below the beard or in the armpit or near the ribs
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is on feet, put it or prick at the sides of the body.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the incision with his right hand, and puts the curvature between his two fingers of the left hand, and pushes it gently with all his hand, and put the incision in any one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the hollow place;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the incision:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then place against another bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extraction is even.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then make it even by moving it from one side to the other, so that it moves easily, and let the bones be toothed so that they hold, as is shown here.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, anoint the bail with some of its oil, and put it into that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if none remain, put this bone or higher up its place, and do this until it comes all out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening.
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	then you must envelop it in a cloth, as long as it persists;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then the bandage at the joint of the foot or at the ankle, and so you must do in the other hand, and for two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the joint of the child is swollen and it protrudes, or there is a sharp point assembled.
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two, and making the chief and draw out the water.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you will do it with the instrument which is called “almidach”, because the form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus same, do if the child has a great head naturally;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then draw out the bones with pliers,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the shoulder jumps back and is forced into place, it may be split open as long as the moisture which is or worse has come out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be moved, cut it into pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you should pierce it until the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on his feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is lodged in the belly or in the breast, then it is necessary that you draw it out with i.e., wrap it wrapped around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture which is there dries up;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are dislocated and the head remains,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	then push the bail his hand into the marrow, and pull it up to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then it puts one or two, and the skin will become
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the abscess is narrowed because of the heat that has come, it does not need to be worked on
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	but rather it is necessary to administer moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administer plasters, and soak in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, then administer what we have said in a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one has no power over it, then the thigh shall be treated in parts, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said concerning abscesses which come in the marrow;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if discharge of blood comes, then it shall be put in a sharp restraint, and administer other cures to him.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then conceived another on top of it, and refused the other life.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, it came to her an abscess in her belly, and swelled so much that it opened, and began a great discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long about it, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed greatly because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I wanted to examine the wound, and with my hands touched the bones, as long as the woman was in better health.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I felt the woman for a long time like that, and it seemed to be coming back together slowly from its place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have recorded this chapter for the reason that, when masters find a strange thing, they may know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to bring the bone back into its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the clamp, as we have found in the books; and to two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be i.e. two finger widths wide, and the edge of the trees i.e. must, and long one palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and among the two i.e. limbs be two fastenings of this same tube, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two fastenings are put in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pliers;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and has two shoulders two joints, as you see, of one palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see to open the vagina with all the instruments, so make the woman sit on one bed, the feet apart and the legs open,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two instruments joined together in the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with all the instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the patient does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all surmounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the eyes have appeared them, so much it is more hasty the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you do not have appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, then it behooves you to command the woman that she retain her breath, and then make her sneeze of condiment, and restrain her hands to the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she leaps through this, well is it.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If this does not work, take one pot and make a hole or lid in it, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialgine, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or none of them, be cooked or put in water over the fire; then put one end of a rope or perforated pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	And steam it until the vapors come from within the marsh; then make it sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part jumps hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this cure and is not better, as you command the nurse to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in a poultice of alum, and then puts it in the wound.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and grasps the second bone; and when she has found it, she seizes it and extends it little by little straight, so that the marrow does not fall out during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved gently to and fro, and then pulled; so it will come out and disengage.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the marrow is tight, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not of all that we have said, so guard that you do not use for milking;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that the one that is at the mouth of the mare, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then enema it with ointment tetra pharmacon;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she will bear and put it back in, and come forward; but nonetheless, when she bears it if there comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and makes the patient pale.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then fumigations suitable to this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument which one uses to fumigate the woman at childbirth retention is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like a cage in appearance, and one puts the subtle head inside the body, and the wide shoulders above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over the embers, and the rag as long as it is smoked, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but it is stopped by subtle things.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore it befits the midwife that she pierce that thing at its proper place, and do not pierce it with sharp instrument, and guard the incision so that she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put upon it a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put in the opening a piece of lead, and let him lay still for a day, and remove it when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this numbness comes from the closing of a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that closure; if it is cured, as we have said about the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are knotted, and larger than those that come from near the outer foundation, or in the space of the two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one fistula or more; and when that knotting is old, it works, and still damp moisture white or subtle bows,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And at times these fistulas are present; and they are known by those who have them either by discharge or windiness when the patient defecates, and by chance sometimes one jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that reach to the bladder and halfway up the penis; and extend to the groin joint, and to the buttock.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the fistula that is penetrating at the foundation, and not penetrating:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and that you place your two index fingers or foundation, and insert a thin needle of iron or steel into the fistula when it has no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, put there a tent of fine lead or one hair of horse, as long as you feel the tent or the hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out of the opening or by windiness or hernia, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary tract, then urine leaks out and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced to the juncture of the hip, then the tendon comes to its place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain is in the surrounding area, then it is that it has bowed inward, and it does not merit medicine nor treatment by ointment.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these Persian fistulas there is no cure but labor, and vanity of the foolish remedies that intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In those that are neither Persian nor ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the base, then it is necessary that you put your index finger there;
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel that the tent has pierced it; and whether it is uncovered or you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then you know it is pierced;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said, however, that one can well heal none of them, but this rarely happens;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help one gives them, if one carefully applies the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and it completely bakes the fistula, as far as it reaches the base; and do this 2 or 3 times, as long as you know that these charcoal-like growths are burned, which resemble the quill of an eye;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure of wets tents in butter, as long as that char is wet, then the cure of ointment binding flesh and joining.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, it is well. If not, it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters and does not pierce to the bottom which is the foundation, and there is between your bottom and the tent a thick covering of flesh or fascia, and you see the fistula at this which follows the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and push forward before the tent, and then cauterize afterward, as far as it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	And will be delivered the tent, and will fall; then define those charted ones that seem a feather of bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sans [meaning unclear] vaints, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cautery of fire assembles two good things: that is to say, the burning of those joined charted ones, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure with tents moistened in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound is bowed [meaning concave], and the charted ones are burned in the bottom;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound of the eyelids by applying hard dried flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the base, and is removed from the body, then you put on your own skin or foundation, and inquire about this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between two and three is the cloth or silk or skin, or it is near to piercing, then there is only a way of trust and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in cutting, that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and let the evacuations come by the natural way.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound after it is cut close to the foundation, or by tent or another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	Then make up the flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part outside the foundation; so it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is or lies against the foundation near the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one twisted thread into two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin of the base inside, then extract the thread from that one pierced, just as you put your doe or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	And treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to another, and let it be for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And restrain it no more times, until the threads close these gaps that are between two, and they stick together.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound until it is joined and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a lance for the fistula if it is too deeply embedded, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spatula used for making a fistula should be very smooth and one-edged;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, for those that one does not cut, those that one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are according to 2 manners: or they are within the foundation, as much as grains of resin, and there are small and large, and in short they bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and moreover there or a drop of clear water or a drop of blood, and have the color of the body
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure of those who have them within the foundation, if it is that you command the patient to stretch for air in chambers, as long as the foundations are inflamed and the threads appear
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and can grasp it with forceps, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with one drapery, or with cotton, or from a piece of felt
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and hold them with your two hands, then cut them, and put some hot powder on the place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the base cannot be discharged, then have the patient take a harsh and biting enema to wash what is at the base so that it can come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	And if the patient does not complain and if the thread is loose from the base, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is that you prick them with your finger or tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is fitting that you administer the suture in this manner: take one twisted thread and put it in a needle, then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce through from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do this with all the others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place on the foundation one piece of cloth moistened in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest until they heal, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment until they are sound.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying of the veins in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	Then you should scrape it at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail, leaving it to dry.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then the cure as long as he is healed as it is fitting.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot heal, then the scraping begins again stronger than before, until it heals well, and is scraped.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure as long as it is healed.
dou fremit	for trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Ant is a small appearance fashioned before the body, and goes much deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And at times it finds him cold, and feels one as dead from fright, and comes throughout the body, and more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a rod of goose feather, or a raven's feather strong, and put that rod on the fright, until the circles redden the fright all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand on all the rod until you scrape all around the fright, and put it deep, and pull out the fright from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a hound of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, but to keep at the two, and move pressing And if you see, so cauterize the groove, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time is made clister of silver or brass, or iron melted or meshed; and no time is made of these instruments small and great, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those which one administers in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is inside pierced; and on one side two holes, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and is the belly where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And between each opening one must put a distance, then put in each opening one strong thread of twisted thread in ten or more, and assemble the belly as if it were a ram;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside, the patient holds the instrument before with a strong thread, then administer a clyster; and this is the form of the circle;
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister compresses it with his two hands together, until it is all full, then withdraw the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the side;
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to issue, so let it sleep as much as it can; and if it sleeps one night entirely, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him with the sickness of a falling belly, and the medicine hastens to issue, so restart it until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at their base, or an abscess, so be the enema as subtle as for one child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin should be restrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and of medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and cutting of sword and knife, or spear or club or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head simple, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, if one takes care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt greatly of abscess hot: if the one makes it to bleed from the cephalic itself even if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the bleeding on the contrary of the sunken part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient overindulgence of wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not wish to heal, then let him moderate his meat and drink no wine nor eat any meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in wine stich.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess hot, then put on the wound, if it is fresh to all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little after.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he has moved the arm, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together with tents, then bring them together with sutures, just as I shall say for wounds of the belly, by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed bone, and hangs, and holds only by one piece, then cut it away. Then cure the wound with medicine, and restore tough flesh in its place of skin
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and wheat cooked, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find yourself with rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, so cut away all the rot, and throw it away, then cure.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then seize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which binds as soon as the wound has closed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply it to the wound, and hold it in place firmly, until it dries well and joins together with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then cover it well, and leave it without unbinding it, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time should one make this with only quicklime when they lack incense or dragon's blood, but that the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the art has moved the wound, even in this state, do not put any of this powder there.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But put on some ointment made from boiled herbs, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it is moist.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then care for it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here afterwards about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but leave it to heal, and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let it be the medicine sweet, as warm water washed and mixed with rose oil, and cooked water also in sweet water
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so stitch it and bind it with bandages, then care for it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of pus, then pierce or lower than that.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and there comes a flow of blood, then stop it, and close it up, and cauterize it if that is necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the veins, and the conduit is kept, because that is where the meat goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	So cut the heart above the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but place it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the restraint is applied, and it is left for some days, then it is treated with ointment dressings until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then so be it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, then treat them all as best you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound heals.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be cleansed and aligned the opening;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, put powder on top of the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look at whether from the wound there are windinesses as the patient breathes; you know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, do not put any powder to it in the first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not stay within.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the heart, and comfort the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put attractive ointment, and bind it 2 times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes no spasm, nor evil trembling of heart nor dragging of the arm;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good arrangements, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it then with bandages and other dressings, as long as it heals;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and work, know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper, or on the back, treat it as that which is before.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, use powder; and if it is deep into the bone and has broken pieces, then treat the wound and the fractured bones if they are severed;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not severed, let the wound rot, so that it will ease extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds as other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The displacement of the belly is great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound sometimes the intestine or the nerve of the intestines jumps out, by which the intrusion of others;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes worse the small wound than the large.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	for this reason one puts back the intestines in, only if they are put back hot and cold;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they go back in more difficultly,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and for this reason the small wound is worse, for this reason one resets the intestine to its place more than others two;
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the sutures of other wounds of the body and two other special sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nonetheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine has come out
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if it needs to be closed, then it is done by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or by the smallness of the wound, as we have said
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or a soft cloth in tepid water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook it in water,  squinting and cypress and spice,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestines until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this makes it tight, and it moves just a little bit to loosen.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or wine and let them be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by these is aligned the entrance to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a hole in the wound with the instrument with which one treats hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to move the waist
