que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut into it without great necessity
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it's cut inward at the curve and outward not, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put it back in according to its natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able, because this is important.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	If it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if you put the head and pelvis higher than the lower parts.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you put your attention to that the sunken part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is fitting to administer what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds apply that which has appeared to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then place in your hands one minister piteous that holds all the fracture with his hand
et assemble les levres;	and assembles the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and that you pierce a needle or more, according to the quantity and width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound 1. that is, a space, and there insert a needle where it has 1. good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the 2. heads of the skin with the 2. heads of the shaft,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is below the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the 2 heads of the shaft together in the 4;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then the strain of a double thread wrapped around the needle of 2 parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the 2 heads of the wound evenly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave 1/2 a space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread like you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing this according to what you need of needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be medium-sized, between fine and coarse,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the fine needles cut all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason they must be shortened
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not proper to put the needles too far from the flesh and skin
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not cut and open the wound before the suture
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the needles so that they don't prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I place tents or drapes on the shoulder of the needles to keep them from moving
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them stay until the wound is closed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for one needle or two are sufficient
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two cheeks of the skin and the two cheeks of the fascia together with a needle on which there is one strong medium thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have pierced these four cheeks together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then you shall pull the needle to the part where you began, in the manner on which one sews the garments;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a man's finger.
ceste costure sevent li home,	This stitch is suited for a man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound that one had in his abdomen,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was mangled by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and was the wound more than a palm wide.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	And it was of intestines well two palms wide.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine after it had been  24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sutured up to the 15th day, and it healed, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the healers thought he would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in one place where none could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put half a finger more on the wound with old cotton twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it was cured.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and push it from the outside part to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it pierces the flesh right through, lead it with your thumb or where you inserted the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch as the furrier does furs
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the thread on one side, and take it back on the other, as long as the stitching is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galen says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like that which some make, who join together the two parts naturally.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the heads to the other head, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	Insert a needle or head of a mirach close by, and make him feel it only,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two heads of the syfac;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make him feel it from the outside part to the inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the two shoulders
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make one feel each of the outer part until that inside, in two other shoulders of the miracle that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common way to suture and the most usual.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	The Galicians say this word, and no one testifies it
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in each
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more grievous than other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the flesh has been moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put the intestine back in and stitch it together, then put powder on it that will heal flesh
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the flesh has been moved, then put some ointment on top of it, as long as the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and be joined the fascia, and the membrane.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you lack medicines, put upon it, as soon as it begins to fester, old cloth,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need another medicine in many cases than when wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not make community with principal members.
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is proper that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of thyme, or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the angles and under the buttocks.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or rot in his bowels, and it happens many times.
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if black wine enemas are given, and similarly if the rot comes as far as the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it is pierced inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine that is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is rotting,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is for the placement of the veins that they are, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back in as quickly as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned to a worm or black, then you must tie the place that is black, so that blood doesn't flow from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound up to outward in order to align the extraction when the bone falls and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can, restore in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	for that I see that one man was pierced in the belly of a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and from it there were excrement and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I made the cure according to what I could, and did not cease to work until it was healed, and the bones joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it join together, I feared that the patient had badly in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no ill, but he remained in better dispositions, and ate and drank;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they said any experimentors that when he had a small wound in the intestine, he must be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take fresh threads with large needles, then assemble the lips of the wound
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	And when the thread has covered the mouth, place it upon the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it draws its mouth together
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cut the thread, and it holds so that it cannot untie
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put one other fragment after it in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered
et cout la plaie.	and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That chief if it burns in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can bind the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine thread that is very bare,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread i.e., a thread of fine linen twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and wind it in the opening;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching of remedies is not outside according to the way of hope and expectancy;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the inner bowels, there is nothing but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and also when it is pulled back and bent.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a hardened, white knot, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also pulled back like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in its clarity it is bent, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes much, and sometimes enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is only due to one of the 8 causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or for its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside it, and on the lips, that does not allow flesh to be born;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the material is spoiled, and the quality is bad;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	when the medicine is not good in the cure
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late in digestion, and slow in healing, and inflated by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I make you know the cure of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the liver, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that it comes to the property of the principal limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are this way are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it known, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, if curved.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then surround it with a subtle tent of wool.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for wool can be molded to follow its twisting shape;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula is open by hand and you cannot well cover it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it by one of its openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture passes from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then carefully probe it with your power, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and whether it is closed up properly,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask well the patient of the pain that he feels at the pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if the blow according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and bone being the cause and the characts corrupted that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep and straight, then you should cut it deeper, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then put soaked tents in a hot poultice, and push them to the top of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medication corrodes the superfluity that is lodged at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then he places ointment for healing flesh, as long as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	And if it is not healthy by this means, then cauterize it as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve grazes or touches principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so wash it as long as the corruption is all removed
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with things that heal flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it doesn't heal and returns bent like before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone far enough.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if uncovered and want as long as you are at the bottom
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	If there is no other means than to let nature have its way;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	And if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones,  extract them all thoroughly, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if it copes with moisture and flesh, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something preventing rotting,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it remain until the flesh rots around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and therefore they will have more easily the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove only the corruption until the blackness is entirely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of corruption, and comes to the flesh of the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it must be cut and covered all until the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to one man in his leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was one youth about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the materials came to the leg, and was swollen with a large abscess, and had no outer cause to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physicians by their folly operated so much that the abscess opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they removed much of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came much pus that all was flowing out, wet and from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a while they care for  two years, and there is no sage in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until that I came to be called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they cured him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those who were being treated through the punctures of great body parts.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man was becoming red, and it had a citron color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then leaned in, and poked into one of the holes until I discovered part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came right up to the inside bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was that one who showed me of the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was not another corruption, except for that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medications of softening by long time, and could not join (or heal);
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I recommenced, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then took it out, and I lamented that I could not join (or heal) the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could no more than I coped to one palm of the bone, and the traitor was to all its flesh.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines; and he became healed and well quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to begin the work except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	Because for the evacuation of blood often, but he was healed completely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in the place of the bone there grew a hard flesh, and he was of good disposition and had no annoyance or contrary at all, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one linen cloth, and bind it to the head of the bone that is open.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	And instruct any one to stretch it upward
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	And put another linen bandage larger than the first linen, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh down.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh in the place where you see to be, so that the skin does not cover the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place one splint or a board under the bone so as to cover the corrupted flesh
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to be as careful as one can see and feel the corruption, and to be still another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the flesh completely; then place one splint under,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then be from one part to the other the corruption, and be the suture of the long corruption i.e. point, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, so cut the corrupted joint, and suture the bone where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else to be cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or in the finger of the foot, then this thing is very strong;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, how it opens to you
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in every way that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the instruments and threads for covering these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare for each kind of operation its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	So consider the instrument which you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can come out due to inside or outside causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and they are of no use,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by these from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; if you hurry about the cover,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the top of the back, if it [is] covered, and do not let him have any space to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, cover it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and does not merit treatment other than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And so do this when the corrosion comes or where it hurts: if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes where it hurts, cut all of the pain;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister to the lower ligament, and another minister to the upper ligament,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you shall cut away the flesh that is between the two ligaments one span wide, until the bone be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cover or clothe it, and put on each side one sheet of linen, so that the sore does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And may another lesion and abscess come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place thoroughly,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on any restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb hurt with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it happened to one man in his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion first came in his heel of the foot, until it spread throughout the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corrosion, he tried to cover his foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And long afterwards it returned, the corrosion in his hand, and he came to me
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things which are pounced upon after the purification of the body, and cannot cease the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he begged that I would cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of counteracting the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And also beware if he cuts his hand, that he does not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the virtue of man was weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And took it upon himself to cover his hand, and became healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have recounted this tale for no other reason than so that one can do otherwise if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to a head, and it lasts so long that it creates great swelling.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then breaks open and bursts, and the swelling goes out, and the place remains as though it were a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin that is on top is as thin as one fine linen cloth
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach down to the bone or to the nerve, and such a sickness is called "healthy."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called “fistula”;
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so lengthened that it comes as far as the bone, then it is called “fistula”;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure of this is that you cut that skin all around, and also when it is thinned out, just like a piece of cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not get worse for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if the breasts are large, and the bowel inside smells foul.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then administer a clyster made with Egyptian medicine, which is prepared as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take thus, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put to cook in one vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in clysters the rectum, and restrain the protrusion;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine rest for 2 hours, then remove it by squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the chest is defined, and the fear is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time is a clysterized of ashes water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine isn't present, and it is that you gather ashes from vine wood, and pour water above
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then the flow, and in a clyster, until you know that the breasts are well moistened.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then clyster them with water and honey where there is a pinch of litharge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you may clyster them with honey and mellowed wine, for honey has the property of purifying and cleansing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the flesh hard;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the enema of those that make flesh grow in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you apply a plaster of this kind, and it is made with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clysterize him with certain medicines and unguents, of which I have said the properties or treat the unguents
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the chest is small, and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then widen it with iron a little, and place inside a tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or ointment basilum, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	And if the wound is too wide, sew it so that only the place where the clyster may enter remains open.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the opening which is above is gaping, close it or stitch it lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the wound is in good repair, do not let any flesh be drawn in;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot close the opening below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	If it is prepared in such a way that the bowel goes to the lowest place it exists.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bowel is full, if one does not allow entrails to be let out.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast as you wish.
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If it is prepared in such a way: that the bowel goes gently down, and nothing from the bowel remains;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the chest
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and extend it over that is a linen sheet that covers the entire chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then wrap with forces in place the opening of the chest that is one palm wider than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then extend ointment over another sheet according to the quantity of the opening,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the opening of the chest to align the rib, and do not remove the large cloth outside except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And he who is outside the opening of the chest, often remove to remove the rib.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And know what comes from the rib, if it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take ward if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been spread in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps over the wound of the chest,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is healed already, and approach the healthy ones;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then untie it in the morning, or every third day, and when you untie the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change one other bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed indigestion after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venoms cut after a long time, so do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health approaches. For there are men whose healing is slow in their wounds, and some who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if a breast lies bowed indigestion after many days, know that the breast does not heal well;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to heal, and are swollen, apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as ointment of diaphana, because it contains a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphana ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the essence of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then pour it and use it; and those same made honey cooked mixed,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when inflammation has defined
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then you glue it onto a cloth, and put it on the chest, and every time one administers a long licorice stick
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the lily of heaven, which is also like flour of violets and centaury.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in using simple or compound remedies: grind them up and make a powder from it, and place it on the honey that I have said, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is elongated, and isn't healed by this treatment
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has entered deeply, and makes an impression in the bone, or hard members, or limbs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the wound of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the ankle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panace is an abscess that arises beneath the ankle of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or in the foot, or perhaps arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and care is not taken, then comes one abscess after another,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they dig and set the bone until it reaches the root of the joint, and perhaps they break it completely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion comes to the bone, until there is pain and suppuration, and the joint is loose, and the color is livid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then you must cut away all the superfluity that is hanging from the joint
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the joint is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the joint adheres to the flesh, and it begins to prick, and the skin
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a rag under the joint where it pricks the flesh
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And the end on top, and cut this flesh subtly and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And put on top the remaining flesh with medicines burning and corrosive to remove all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with dressings until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and treat it, because as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the two bones to be corrupted, cut it in one of them as it has been said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken and bruised, and it causes great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the angle with a spatula by cutting crosswise on top,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and guard that the blade does not come near the flesh that is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the hand's source
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints that are born in some men's hands by chance are all fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	And by chance there is some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And none of these grow at the root of the joint, where the birth is in no one's two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born in neither one of the two does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And he who is born at the joint of the two, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Whoever is born at the root of the joint, he is difficult to cure; so you must be careful when cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or is at the end of his buttock, you should first cut away the rounded flesh up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then set the bone to a suitable silk, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The bandages that come to two together come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is fitting that you set that suture, so that the parts repay according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil, so that they do not adhere.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	and you put between two pieces of subtle splint, until the bones are joined, as it is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The joining comes to none of his two with the palm, if he copes that joining as it is fitting.
Des vils	Of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Vices are veins large and full of melancholic superfluities, that come in more than one member of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often happens in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging of colocynth, and then the healing of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is thus in two ways: one is with the cup and drawing out black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the vein and draw all of it out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The waist is thus treated in this manner: first raise the leg of hot water very much, until the thick flesh is softened.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then pull the leg of the patient from above the hip to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, of a wide size.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then remove and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much flesh as the virtue of the patient can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the wound, and instruct him to apply a poultice of black ointment;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of the leg is done this way: raise the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and raise the leg from hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut the place of the vein long from the arm to the knee, or in the part below at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then work the skin with the scalpel, and scrape the vein on each side until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white rope;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the point below, until it is lifted from the skin, and then cut it lightly with the scalpel,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then the cut in one other place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it to the root, as you have done, and put it in another needle, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another piece, or more if you need it, then lift and cut at the two points of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift until the second piece; then extract piece by piece until it is completely free, then cut;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, put a needle at its end to a strong doubled thread
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it out, and put beneath it one weight, and turn your hand from one side and the other, as long as it comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep that it does not break, for if it breaks, then one cannot draw it out nor lift it, and it brings annoyance to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it all out, put on the wound's place wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the bone is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if it is necessary that you split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one covers the bone is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cover the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cover the vein, but be gross as we have said, and here is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where there do not grow herbs nor trees, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the rotting that comes from beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from within the body of serpents and worms, lodged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it changes its color, and the vein begins to emerge, as if the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder is opened, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to two fingers in width, and tie it
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and every time that it feels any pain in the outside part, wrap it again around the plank, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely grown.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, and bring an abscess and putrefaction there, and a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore for that reason it is necessary that it be treated carefully and bit by bit until the head, and nothing of it remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein when it is treated is five palms long, or ten.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me once, whose arm was out 10 palms long, and when you cut it, it shoots 1  arrow or more, and pierces it to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all is out; and it should be emptied the matter which is inside, and administer to its place medicines preventing corruption any day, then cure it like the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at times to this vein hands reins, and also when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes out much blood, and from which it jumps reins; cure therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This sickness is called in our land "ox disease" because it happens many times to oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it well at the change of limb to limb, as long as it breaks through the skin where it goes and leaps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by rot from certain humors, such as worms and lice and ascarids in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its malice, because when it travels through the body, it ascends to the head and comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and milked, there is no escape but when it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So then it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong ligature very tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then cut above it and bring out the cord, and if the nerve is caught in the flesh, and you do not find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, then restrain below it the eyebrow forming, then cut above, and the track further.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body of medicinal solutions for the bad humors corrupted,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if there are sores from rotting meats.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This sickness is called "vakir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and just a little after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything, just like living silver when it is cut from its place;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that spot and goes into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it spreads throughout the body until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it returned again around her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved so from limb to limb, because I have never seen this sickness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I have seen many who well had the pain move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have never seen it like this, as I see in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and uncovered veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this appears that constrained windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see curing this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the lump above and below is evenly spread out, and then cut on top until that constrained windiness at the place has gone away;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the care of those who expel the wind, such as pills of viper and pills of serpent, and similar ones.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small ones, and hairy, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And those that fall in any member fall in two ways: or in the principal member it falls,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls therefore in any place of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you take care in the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the soft tissue which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when eye scotomata and soddenness and eversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps this without force from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jump from the wound moisture white seeming to boils, and in jump also as burnt of flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appear to you, then hold from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, is that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the seventh moves as the arm, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the saette that never moves is that without plains of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and throws great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perchance it leaps out of the wound something undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and leaps out no point of straw through the gut path, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine leaks out and comes outside, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and the similar members, are saved according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that reason that you would do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man with an arrow in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and drew it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without feeling anything at all.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And throw it to a game an arrow that fell in the fat of the eye under the paper down,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck, and could not reach except its point towards the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and it was the arrow great as an archer's, with all i. one light iron without ears; the game was unharmed and did not suffer any ill happening.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And throw an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and it was the Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was the beards, and I skillfully led it until I betrayed it, and it was healed for the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I betrayed an arrow in one man, that it was in his chest or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then when he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and I loosened it, and I betrayed it further, and there was no bad accident.
