Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man to whom an arrow fell or back, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any pain in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and stay thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow in the king of lords'  a man, that was lodged in-between his ribs.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly reclining towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to treat him after it had lodged for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it with all of a subtle tent, and did not feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt tingling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the spot a lead plaster digestive, because the  area did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared to me the joints of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the plaster on immediately that day, and sutured the wound directly, and kept the patient there a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow i.e. one day within his flesh; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine by hand immediately, for as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and try it, and feel the head of the arrow which is straightening in place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust it in the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it pierced well the ends for .iiij. months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I enlarged the wound so that I put it in the pliers, and mine on one side and the other, and it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore, do not cease to tinker and devise ways of instruments, until I took one day well-made pliers.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I treated it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it, therefore, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or you have been told the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your cure on those which I do not say, because the books cannot take everything in;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well to a very small thing, and on those which are present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and nine instruments, at the descending of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are not from the limbs where they are fixed except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those that go beyond where they enter, are arrows that enter into the flesh, and do not come out at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, let it remain as long as the flesh is sore around it, and ease the exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is lodged in the bone, and it cannot come out, then leave it as such for several days, and moisten it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, then pierce around it to the entire i. forest subtle, as long as the skin around it is enlarged, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not treat it, but leave it as long as it is equal after several days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes to the bone it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come to the bone .
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient stays for some days without bad accident, then the cure will be easy.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot be pulled out, then administer poultices as I told you; then treat the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then cover the whole wound.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then treat it with no suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you cannot by the widening of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then widen it as much as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at its end with which it holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you remove the shaft that is stuck in two parts as much as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and skillfully so that you do not break the arrow but rather draw it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then bring it up until the joint is warm, then treat it, for the extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding contradicts you, then administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against cutting the nerve and the vein, and put anything you can to draw out the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether quickly or slowly, whether firmly or gently; and set the patient according to the form that it was in when the arrow hit him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help if it can be done, and if you cannot, put it according to how the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or where one sees nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in place if one sees or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, as much as the tongs can take, and then extract it; if it leaps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push it out with the whole shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft has broken, and you see to administer pushing, then administer one instrument with a head,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged, put one instrument with a point entering it, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is encircled, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls into the groin or belly or bladder or ribcage, and it is near, and you can cut above it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And keep from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary is.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the care until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to an eye beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the tip of a hair is like the quill of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To insert at the point of the arrow, as this is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for inserting and holding is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one is healed there are thirty-one, of which the head has sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: two veins that are behind the ears, called the two "herbechs".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is taken from the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are on the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly opened are five in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is on the inside of the left side of the body, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called "basilic", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the outside of the body,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is on the fossa
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is the one from which blood is drawn, which clearly opens on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphenous vein is the one between the ring finger and little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot is, there are three veins: one of which is below the curvature of the pouch of the left hipbone;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "ness," which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the veins that are after the ears if it helps with old catarrh, and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the  vein, as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck to a splint.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then place it over your back, and where you feel the pulse below your back, press down there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand along the whole vein upwards;
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cup and the skin and the vein well two fingers through, and make blood flow as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and bind it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The  draining of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for an old migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sudden, and habitual eye diseases, and to the body of the sharp tears eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of blood are like I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient strains his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below his back, and then grasps it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lightly raise the heart above the vein to your right index, and thrust the needle below.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and raise the vein upwards, and the cup, as you have done with two other veins, and make a correct drawing of blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then untie the patient, and put your right hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form the bandage, and leave it on until it is healed; and we have spoken of this before and of their cutting and extraction, as the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bloodletting of the vein of the forehead is as valuable as the bloodletting of the cephalic for illnesses of the face ancient, and migraine, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the qualities of this are that the patient strains their neck twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor," whose shape is here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and hold steady with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then tie up the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed, and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not right that the flames be too thick; and to heal across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and the chin, and the cheek, and the eyelid, and illnesses of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their healing are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with a bandage, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the healthy flesh is cut, and it should be like the length of a flame, a bit wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The opening of the vein for the purpose of letting blood is good for fever, for  inflammation, and for diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the qualities of the vein are such that the patient tightens his neck, then pulls his chin to your left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and takes a subtle long flame, and puts it between the two nostrils
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well enough, and blood will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it flow too much, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two veins helps in the treatment of the spleen, and at the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and itching, and corrosion, and herpes, and inflammations;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the blood are that the patient draws his neck out from under both, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on one stool,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then heal the vein with a long incision, then treat the blood appropriately, as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then redo the other part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and restrain both veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	So that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, that the wound be healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of healing of veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips from above helps to heal in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and to wounds and sores.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you know them by this that they are black, and by this that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore, one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you take the largest of each part, and also make two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the vein below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein below the tongue is helpful after the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of the vein are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks under on each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore feel one and both, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm which one commonly feels are felt in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or they prick at all  one finger's breadth wide, or olive-shaped subtle as you feel trenches, and is called "anesis";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening the veins that are heavy with abundant visible blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for opening veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bloodletter to bleed skillfully, and that he should avoid the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it behooves him to stop it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and flame must not be piercing but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you restrain it, and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no vein of it, or you make in its place the vein in the arm: it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cut with the flame knife, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see to know the place of the sinew, then it is right that you extract the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame asleep;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and guard that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place inflamed, because it is from the artery: therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise upwards as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Haste yourself therefore, and put your knee upon length, then remove your knee if it does not stain, which many times happen.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Bind his arm, and leave it thus, and do not move it the patient; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stained, and it weeps, and the medicine is not present, then cover the artery if it opens, for the head of the retraction; and stain the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a rind of fig, and make it, and take one of the halves and tie upon well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding is stopped, that is good; if not, treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of the blood is not always easy in many situations because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood from the vein in the middle helps treat blood from the head above and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the healer that he search for the nerve which is below, and if he does not find it too much, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and he inflames it and the healer's hands are burned, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtlety, then you must heal it with the instrument of the nail; and grasp the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make a cut along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to vein by pricking it in the olive branch or the myrtle branch, because it is the safest of all veins, because it does not have nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and nothing grieves if it fails the first time, and one begins again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance it swells for some men, even if it fails the first time, but it does not grieve.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The qualities of blood are according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bloodletting, is that it is administered only to preserve health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off diseases to come;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and that the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are or ought to be: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must bleed at the beginning of Lent in spring, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one must bleed the first day or the third, after two or three hours or a day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick does not have a set time, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and in all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not behoove to bleed children until fourteen years, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when some want to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have much phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous putrid matter to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not bleed those who are too full of meat, nor who are drunk, as long as they are intoxicated, nor the dropsy-afflicted.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if it were to worsen after colic passion and vomiting and stomach pain, and multiplication of labor in women, and childbirth, and wakefulness and fasting, and whatever through all virtue, or by things of the weapon or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly regulate the humors, if it is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have their power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtly regulate the blood;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and drain the vein of the lower third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself on that day of labor, and of pricking, and of lust, and of similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be tied and joyful, and let the healer's hands be higher than those who are healed, and rub the arm two or three times
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then draw the linen upward in the middle, for when it is too stretched out or pulled, then it cannot be corrected without injury.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub that place with your hands until the veins swell up and you feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the vein with a drop of old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand upon that vein below its place where he wants to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the vein may not be felt and feel like it is being pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that swell as ropes when bled, and some that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the cautery upon it, it retracts from the cautery and cannot open the vein, and thus is this type
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, for this reason it is necessary that the healers be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, it is restarted once more a little below where it was or above carefully, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient feels anxious, let him rest for one or two days, and don't bind his arm at all:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for it may happen that an abscess comes to a head; nor does he enter into the bath, then restart the bloodletting if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the vein is too thin and you doubt that it isn't as much blood as you see, then fire in that same opening all the way to the tip straight.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work a little gently, so that the eyes are inflamed; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place inflamed, then do not begin bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil on it, because it soothes the body of blood, and is mixed in this place with the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing happens with a triangle and a bow of theirs, when it is put on the place; so subtle is its feel and it separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes an abscess that is large, which happens often, even when it is not drained except for the time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you hasten and put on top the sponge moistened in water and with some hot wine, and restrain it an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the exit of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days no blackness or greening, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put upon anything of aloes or frankincense  put back into juice of calamint, wormwood, or semblance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance at the saint's basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft at the compression of the hand, then is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, I advise you that you do not put upon it anything of what we have said, because perhaps a vein lies within; but make one dry plaster to harden the place, then cure with another cure, until it be healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it shrink until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it befits him who is weak and ill, and has need of bloodletting, that one makes a wider wound for him, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to him who is feeble, do the opposite, and it befits him to bleed little and often, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding is safe from the depletion of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is worth more than bleeding long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body needs to be opened for bloodletting, it is appropriate to give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, treat him with blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, give him moist bread before bloodletting in syrup of quince, or in syrup of honey aromatic with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and syrup well-scented.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during bloodletting, after the issue of some blood, it is appropriate that he smells broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use of other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the opening of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed other times if necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he should bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another place, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because he has much blood in his body that is already exhausted, and brings fever; so it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the opening until it flows into portions.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you have treated all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his pulses when he is healthy, that death may not come in place of pain
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not proper when you see  the arm to be loosened, and make blood flow a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press forcefully upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	but if it is curved, have him extend his arm carefully, for otherwise it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it stay until it heals the second time; or you prick it at the tip of the flame, as long as the vein that is frozen by being pricked does not return.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on top I. part of boiled oil, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, leave it and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is a need to draw blood for the second time, let it heal in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein from which blood is drawn from the arm is located near the vein of the neck because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of drawing blood is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then blood is drawn now across, not through the wide or long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and let blood be drawn well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drawn from there, then put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood to run in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not immerse the hand in hot water, because one puts it more into winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is safer from all other veins, that there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it is broken out of alignment, and if you cut it through completely, it will not harm anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not press too hard on them for the nerves are all bare of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if it is frozen stiff in the wound and cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and wool on top of the vein to close it well, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of the left hand is good for the disease of mice, and do everything as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The vein of the [soft palate] is good for all diseases that are below the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the bowels, and retention of flowers, and disease of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of this vein are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs over the vein until it becomes warm,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and bind above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	so then take the vein there or one wider, or at the ankle, which you deem best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it on the foot, guard the nerves which are below, and drain it by traversing as when cutting; and let the flames be anethesing.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot draw out blood from it, put the foot in water, and let the vein be emptied well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first incision is necessary, then begin the second one above a little bit, because the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and then do the same with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of fury, and its incision is worth for the pain of the hip when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its incision are that the patient enters or baths in it, and is strained above the ankle four fingers by twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise he does not open the vein; and if it opens, then close it in all the ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, because the skin is dry, and it is very well joined by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then close any opening from the leg or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard against the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make as much bloodletting as you see fit, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and restrain it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of windsucks
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Windsucks are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is heated, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and suction that is done by piercing and drawing blood is done in fourteen parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Of which one is all in the sum of the head; and the other is in the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others in two ribs of the neck; and the windpipe below the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the windpipe at the two shoulders; and the windpipe above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the windpipes in the two arms; and the windpipes in the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups on the two ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, but of the small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore it does not weaken one as much, as one does from a vein bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither to hot nor cold fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it is necessary to suction, or by habit, then let us administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between, and at any time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to sneeze, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see through blood, pus, and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is emitted during the month, we command to vomit after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the vein helps to the great pain of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not right that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this vomiting is in place of the bloodletting of the cephalic vein,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not right for those who are of cold complexion to use it, or who have diarrhea, because it does them much discomfort.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it does not behoove the elderly to use them, nor those who have or fever colds.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are healed by it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The venting on the neck is in place of the healing of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the treatment of pain.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to the fissure of the channel of the palate, and to all, and to repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and then one must not press too hard, because if it is held too tightly, it can cause obstruction in the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The two ribs of the collarbone are worth against pains in the head, and ophthalmia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the healer that he presses his hand when applying it so that he does not cut the artery and there comes a hemorrhage
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosation below the chin is worth against diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for diseases that come from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventilation of the armpits is as good as three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the patient not to prick them too deeply, because they are bare of flesh and full of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids from the foundation, and for diseases of the bowels, and it should be large and of iron so that it needs to well suck; and by chance if it were thin, it would break; and there will make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses of the legs are sucked open well, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the joints; and they are placed in the place of the two shins, and of the two ankles, but all the same they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of placing the cupping glass is that you put it first empty, and suck moderately, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from this doing until you see the skin red and inflamed, and appear the flow of blood; then fix, and replace the cupping glasses, and take heed to the disposition of the body, because there are those who have thick flesh, and porous skin: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a poke deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to prick it two times; the first time to make a subtle way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only make one incision.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we repeat often; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it through with force, and the end is that the veins be pierced deeply.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin and who has porous veins, that you grease the places of the leeches with oil that is refreshing and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is an inflammation, from violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of pumpkin.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is a boil, from cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take wormwood oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one being treated has tender skin and large pores, then it is not appropriate to put any oil on it,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or a similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise from rosemary, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large superfluities, let themselves be raised by old wine, or buckthorn water, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to bleed with a leech before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary for him to be winded when he must be winded and when he is winded.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are healthy are choleric, and if his blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary for him to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the waist, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and minced veal, and  broth meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and mince figs, and quince and small oysters and sparrows;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day that he will be vended, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is fitting to give no man ever garlic or nutmeg before or after the venesection, in order to comfort the limbs principally;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the wine be subtle, but it does not behoove those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed without hurting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the kidneys, and gout, and on the belly and the chest and the hips and the hip, because these members do not suffer to be hurt on their skin.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does it only to draw blood from limb to limb.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we place them on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place suction cups on the belly and chest to diminish the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it is done when one places it upon the liver and the mouse when there is retained windiness.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are administered empty to suck alone; and at no time are they administered together fire, and at no times filled with tepid water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in illnesses of the pleurisy, and in such manner one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable to this have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have 2 fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have or on the cost near the middle 1 small hole, as for putting in a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And be of iron, softened in front so that it does not injure the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a crossbar of iron or steel, to put a burning candle.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let them be large and small according to the ailments and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and of thin people than of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one then place this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	taking a bit of candle wax or one linen cloth, and put it inside the suction cup through the straw that is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light be at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it upon the limb, and you must be on the opening that we have said, so that when one wishes, then into it goes the vapor, and one removes the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take hold of the linen just as before, and repeat it often, if you have need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup, therefore, which is administered in a disease of pleurisy, to all acute pain, there is no stick nor opening, and it is administered only when it is full of fluid, and it is placed upon the limb just so much.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Wounds are not treated except in limbs where it is not possible to apply cupping jars because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in their naked flesh, such as the toes or ears, and similar things.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are that when you find wounds that are in clear fresh water without corruption, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them into water that is not too hot until they are softened and have nothing in their belly;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be purified of vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the poultices;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and blacken, if it is there where one can put a cupping, put it, because this does much good after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the place with ease, and then with water, very well, and then sprinkle it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the place heals too much after the poultices, moisten one cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on, until the swelling subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the sores are multiplied, put on crushed vitriol, or salt, and similar things, until it is stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you put on the spot half of peeled beans, and leave them there until they dry out on the spot, then it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other beans.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the beans do not want to be taken, rub the spot with fresh blood, or put a needle in it until the sores come out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them above, and as soon as they feel the blood, they burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bleeding, powder on a bit of aloe and wool ground together, or ash, and they will now stop bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is concerned with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear friend, that the folly of this chapter lies in the fact that they never saw any of the ancient books or read any letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, knowledge is missing from our land, because I never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing else, except through the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered its science, and through experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have abridged it at the end, and clearly showed the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say here in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise place his understanding, and remain on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the limb is not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold things, that is to say, cold meats, and mutton and veal, and do not drink wine, and do not eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or an expansion of matter in the limb; so return the patient to his first state of government that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.
