And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or they have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and tripe of calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment they recover strength and more quickly the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and the decrepit do not well recover nor join according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but if there is no cure, reset the broken bone, that is, the large tendons that hold it and join the limb together, until it forces as it was before; and do not remove any part of its work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish them with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg, or the thigh, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go awry, and others in sharpening, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to each manner has its engine, and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes to in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And is known the fracture of the bone by those who the parts are twisted, and well open by outside, and sound in the presser of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting nor sound at touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, if there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have twisting, or fracture, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you should not move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes in a circle, and are the two parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them together evenly, so that an abscess does not form.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess forms there, let him not touch it for a day, until the abscess is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it equally to the joint that you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of that one where there are parts; then restrain it, as it is fitting afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone is broken into pieces, if it is of two parts, if it is hands or feet, or to your hand if it is a small member, or to two cords, or to one cord and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you move by all means the additions in their places to the joint as much as you can, and keep that through your work there comes no injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two shoulders of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well; if the dress beautifully, and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work abscess hot and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, so carefully bind the patient that he does not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limb be so secure that he feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	Because when he feels no pain, except at a point, and it is necessary to put him in such a disposition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep that he be put straight, that twisting doesn't come when he is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar: so it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as hips and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard linen cloth, because the wide linen embraces the whole large limb, and restrains it on all sides equally, so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around light bandages, 3 or 4 turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on all the linen, then go above the fracture and restrain it less, so that the fracture is then moved away a bit from the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen little by little, until you feel most of the healthy part, then take another linen cloth, and turn it around directly above the fractured place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and hold it moderately, neither too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first place above
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the swollen ties of linen or cloths, until it is all equal, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then place your well-made pads on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing on the abscess above, which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain the pads on top, and be of half a good width cane properly cut, or from rods which one makes the clews (or stakes), or from palm ribs, and be according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it is necessary for the limb of small size or large size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on the splints just as you did in the first layer, then tie above with a thread evenly, just like in the first layer on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	tighter is applied above, looser below; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in works of fools who make their stitches with cords of linen twisted, and this is a great error, for the stitch cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not be that between each star there is less than two finger's width of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore in the joints of the stitches after the tightening in their healthy places, then put under them pads of linen or wool felt, so that it does not turn blue.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the crushing, and the bones are broken, I will tell you its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to bind all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not fitting to put on bindings immediately rather after five or seven days, or more according to your certainty of abscesses coming hot.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and it is that you take flour that is held at the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, not too light nor too thick, and in use, and this is the common way of the plaster restoring the fracture in many ways, and also to women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three parts each of amber, laudanum, henbane, asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mugwort, ana .x. З.; myrrh and aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; and make it into a powder, and mix it with plenty of egg white; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana. x. z.; myrrh and aloes, ana. viiij. z.; acacia vi. z.; Armenian bolis .x. z., and grind well, and confit with water or the yolk of an egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of ointment for joints and bones that are out of place, and it soothes the pain that comes, and the use of bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and soak it in hot oil and boiled oil, and put it on the sore spot. This plaster does not restore (things) but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removing the pains properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of poultice for the restoration of bone fracture and to lessen the remaining abscess. Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of verbena, each one part; and grind, and boil with wine, and if the limb is cold, add it with moist coriander water, or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of poultice stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of wormwood, and flax seeds, balm, melilot, and elecampane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part; and grind, and boil with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras states in his book that one should put on the broken limb for restoration only a certain made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one must put on the broken limb, to restore, things dry and a little hot, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is good for the lesion and pain: take mugwort and chevolz [likely referring to a type of herb] of oxen cut, or feathers of owl, and vismalve [possibly a type of plant], and seal in equal measure, and grind them, and make it into a plaster and apply.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then remove the bandage a little after, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or the bones have not moved from their place; otherwise do not remove it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the spot, or itching, lack of rest, or swelling, then hasten and remove it, and take off the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and sponge of sea moist [meaning soaked in sea water], and dip it in water, and raise the spot, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a nut, as long as you are sure of the hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and be removed the pain, then recommence the fine binding, and a little ointment, and do not bind it as tightly as before; and subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and the pain and swelling are gone from all of it, and you need ointment and binding, then recommence it, as you did first initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, then do not unbind it for less than 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and never leave it unbound for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and approaches the joining of the flesh together;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	therefore he should be restrained more than before, and you must thicken his flesh as I said above; and if you see the place drying more than necessary, know that there cannot come nourishment
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	therefore arise the hot water then, every time you loosen it, and every third day, and moisten a bit the place;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	for this work therefore shortens the nourishment to the limb, and mends quickly those who do foolishly, that they return the limb twisted: it is bad, and thus is the work dangerous, and I do not see anything else than to let it be and work it straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures are, and diverse forms, and the causes are destined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made from the impact of a sword, and the bone collar all the bone until the shaft which is below the bone, like done high or stick; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword chops the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and is the wound of these two fractures large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impact embedded, or splitting or of the collarbone, or of the heel on bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating, which approaches to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is placed in the bone as finely as a horsehair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and drives the piece of bone inward, and it lies as do the cauldrons when they are heated on the cauldrons; so does the stone enter within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have or whose head is moist bone, such as the head of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and there are in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are severed as if they were stars; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquiry into tents, and by the corrupted cartilage that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of capillary is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs it above, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes becoming redder and more inflamed, and other similar signs in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unfavorable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and the accident we have said comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the tissue that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the broken part as follows: and it is that you prick the head of the wounded person and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more carefully than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if bleeding comes when discovering the bone, or abscess pus, help them as is proper, and that you fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the abscess pus is calmed, and be sure of bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to .ij. ways of work: one way is that you cut at the narrow side in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put .i. other cutting larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of cuttings of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron. And in work lightly, that you do not cut through the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, it is necessary that you pierce it below, so that you administer chisels with drill bits, lest they go beyond the bone; and it must have above its point a rim or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and it is necessary that you have several of these, so that each comes in its place from the width of the bone, so that you have drills for all types of bones; and this is the form of the three kinds of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing below a broken bone is that you put one drill on the bone, and turn with your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the drill elsewhere a little afterward, and do this all around, then cut with the cutting tools the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone with your hand, or with any of the instruments that you have such as pliers; and keep that you do not touch the marrow nor the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you will have pierced the bone, and treated it, then it is necessary that you remove the debris which is stuck to the bone with every instrument similar to a cutting tool, but it is necessary that it be tougher and more subtle than the other cutting tool;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, so lightly to the bones with. i. instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galien says, which is drier; and the load very hard, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put beneath the head of this lens-shaped instrument, from which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut on one part, and it is the pointed part in.ij. sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you gently chop the bone all around, and be well guarded of the cloth that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is stuck to the bone, then gently extract it, because it should be extracted easily without pain and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the broken bone does not pierce to the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to reassemble those asperities, and remove the scales with a fine razor which you must have in various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with large razors, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer care according to its disposition; and this thing is not returned to him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, then it befits you to take i. piece of linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another piece of cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first piece of cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so that you do not injure the wound, then administer above i. other linen, and do not bind it too tightly except that it holds the wound only;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it so for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lily, and powder of quince, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put on the wound, and administer further medicines mixed with honey without mordication;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and guard that the wound be quite clean, that you do not leave there any ointment, nor do you let it gather a crust, because when a crust gathers upon the brain tissue, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; because when one puts on top of this thing biting, it bites upwards.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take guard therefore, if any bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, then it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come there except due to the medicine that one has put on, then it is proper that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue one veil, and put it on the thing.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure of manners of cares that it is fitting, until it be healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the bone above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it be forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is fitting that you put your small finger or point of the bone, and put each fracture inside your index finger, and to the pouch outward, until the bone returns according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and it cannot come to its place, then you should put it equal to the head of a stick, a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, make another one like it, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If this is not possible, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has been calmed, then bandage to the head of the knee ten bandages of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say one must moisten the tents in butter and change them each day. It does not seem well to me, but it is proper that they be moistened with a confection of yolk of egg, and powder of millet; then leave the tent as long as the bone is stiff, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at times one puts down goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is one-half a cloth draped over it, and the wound is held and the patient is breathed upon; or do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the wound as you work on it, put a piece of cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in one part of aqua regia.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess forms there, put a poultice outside, made of sesame flour and incense powder, congealed with egg white, then place light bandages on top, and do not bind it at all.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the bone is small and broken into many pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments, then sew together the split, and treat with things that are healing flesh, and stitching, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the bone, then treat it with splints and place planks inside it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken apart, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outward, and is not broken in two, except for splintering inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then put your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inward, and hold it with the other hand outward, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is broken in two, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or fracture, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put upon the broken jaw cerote, and put upon one double cloth; and put upon the cloth a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on as much as you can, and command the patient that he rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and put plaster on top, of powder from the mill with abundance of egg or sesame flour, after that which you have removed the cerote; and put on light cloth above the plaster, and if the plasters dries, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is sound; many times it is sound in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer that which we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward that no piece of the bone is removed; so subtly of the removal as the instruments suitable to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, so sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on i.  plaster suitable to this, in order to prevent flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times before the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is then when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which is the fractured bone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put each fracture to your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor defect.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be large according to your necessity; and being and light the bone, and restrain the sphere to your hand, so that you put each fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder with force because it comes in its way, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back and put under the shoulder one-half hour, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two, and if you find it broken, then it is necessary that you split above; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any tightening, then cut at one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to guard the syfac:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it seems a spoon, and is not at all hollowed out, and be also wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as it is the break of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of the hot abscess, if cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt hot abscess, then apply the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, moisten one drape in rose oil and in honey and in wine, and put on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on top of the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of egg white, and put light bandages on top, and put a sphere under the hip, if you have need of it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide bandage of one palm in width, then put one double drape on top of bandages and the plaster; then take a subtle board three fingers in width and length, and encircle it with that bandaged cloth, so that the head of the bandage hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy shoulder, and under the injured shoulder; and pull each part together, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, then reward him every day, and when the ligaments slacken, then restrain them;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps one small pillow under the shoulder, to raise the shoulder higher; so it will alleviate the fracture of the collarbone by lifting the shoulder, or tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it except a bad accident happens, up to twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then begin again the plastering if you see that he needs it, and restrain him and leave him so, until he is restored; and it is restored at most in twenty-eight days, and in less time to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder breaks or its long bone is broken in the middle, and one feels it only by touch; therefore, set it according to the figure of the fracture and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on top of the place powder from the mill with abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on .i. double cloth; then put on a broad and fine splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is sticking in any place of the shoulder, use that hair from bandages of linen so that the splint lies evenly; and then restrain it with a very firm bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the limb each day; and every time that it softens, restrain it, and put back evenly the splint if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored in .xx. days or in xxv. And when this number is completed, untie it, and be sure, because it is not bone that comes out easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes outward before and not below the shoulder joint, do it like this, and apply the bone, and make what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The leg is sometimes broken in the middle, but this rarely happens; but it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it bends to the side, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of feeling, and numbness, and perhaps vomits blood, and the skin appears tight on the broken bone, and it hurts a lot.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and he joins the sides of the two bones with his hands, and subtly brings them together in every way that he can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put bandages and bandages above the thin skin of salt, or some other light paste, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around to the back, and tighten it well, and watch every hour the ligature, and if it softens, tighten it; and if it is necessary to loosen it, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hasten and loosen it, and clean what has come there with methods of treatment; then put the bandage back on, and tighten it until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the top inside, and they bend only because they are glassy; and one feels it well upon inquiry on the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put equal the fracture, as it should be. And then place the splint, and restrain it with a stick, if you need it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning inwards, the patient feels very great pain and sharpness, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue; and besides sharp pains, and coughs and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is of serious illness, and the ancients have put great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats which inflate the belly, in order to drive the wind out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one should put suction cups on the area to draw out fluids strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cup draws out the superfluities at the place for the weakness of its disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said one of you should cover the place with a soft wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the air equal, then be cured from the treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that pricks the skin, and there is fear for the patient, then it is necessary to cut on the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath one instrument to guard the cavity; and then one must saw the bone, and draw slightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed. And if an abscess arises, then put soft bandages in rose oil, and put them on the place; and cure while the place of what it should be for an abscess, and lie lying against the ribs where it must be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs to the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that he is mortal in most cases, and if he moves them and feels well when they are pulled and pointed, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one puts care to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if his feet are softened, and if the accidents are in his hands, and on his back there is a swelling and expulsion without will; and when one has him lying on his stomach, there is an expulsion without will. And when he is laid on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot. Know that he is mortal: if he does not labor well in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward him if there is an abscess hot, then put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, as long as it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cover it with the heart; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then cure with an ointment that encourages flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the “head of the cow,” put your pouch in your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and bandage on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are dislocated bones, do it again, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, if it had not been for a little weakening at the head; and making long, and declining to the sides, and comes to the patient pain in the place, and throbbing, and swells what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand upon it, as long as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the form of it; and if the fracture is at the head only, then put equal that fracture, as long as it is in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines to the inside, then make the patient lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it even, put it on the plaster, then put a support of wood or of kerf, and restrain the splinter so that it does not move; and employ the place under the ribs, until the splint is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and restrain it as it should, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take one staff of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two heads with two bands, and raise them up, and make the patient sit on one seat; then place his broken arm on the staff, until it comes to the armpit, and has a bend of staff in the middle, then place on any heavy thing or ministers extend it downward; then put the fingers of your hand together, as long as the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below at all one length, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more distant, bind .i. linen under the fracture, and on the fracture, and extend each of the ministers to its part. And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put .i. linen medium under the bone, and .i. other towards the outside, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the outside, it is necessary to put .i. linen lightly, without labor, until the fracture is equal on the top, and on the outside; then place the fracture equally as it is necessary, and bind, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess does come, do not bind it until .vij. days, and put on linen half in oil and rose oil, until the abscess is calmed; then bind it, and the manner of binding it is that you put the splint on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape, and bind on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents you, or if the bone is not set.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint .i. two of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture .iij. two on each side; then bind on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less far apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the seating of the splints, and the binding, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, then let it remain bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the bandaging, that itching nor swelling does not come to the place, or the dressings cannot come to the limb for that it is too strained. If it agrees, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if none of such accidents comes, then do not unbind it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion plain of wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or of the night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or be softened the bindings; if it agrees by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have before put, in such manner that the food is at first subtle; and when it begins to recover, let it be coarse. And it is customary that the shoulder and leg ought to be taken back in forty days of the whole; and then one must unbind and administer bath and medicines of healing for the place to heal. And if the constriction is ugly and encumbered, then remain unbinding for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two «foscile», because one is small, and that follows the shoulder; and the other is large, and that is below, towards the little hip; perhaps breaks the big foscile alone, or the small, and perhaps andui together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large is broken, so is the healing bad, and more grievously than when they are broken together. If it is the small foscile that is broken alone, then it should be gently stretched, and put straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large foscile, then it should be strained more strongly; and stretched on one cushion, and hold the shoulder of the hand higher than the others, and the little hips lower than the other hips, and let the patient be crossed on himself, and one cushion in front of him higher, that the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch the ministers some arm to the underside to his hand, or to one linen, and another minister to another above. And then put the mirrors straight, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, so put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, so glue it; I mean a bandage of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, that it be not too hard nor too soft; and tie the bandage on top carefully, until the abscesses have subsided. Then remove the cerote, and put the plaster of ground flour with an abundance of egg, then place splints, and let the splint of the fracture be more in depth, and a little wider than the others; and know that it must have six splints or arms in more positions: whether the fracture is in one bone, or two; and tighten it more on top of the fracture than elsewhere, and every day less apart, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages which are on top of the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reward the limb and the bandage after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb with hot water, until the itching is appeased; and leave the limb not even a little rest. And then begin the tightening again, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, so the address.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it happens that the numbing cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and leave so for several days, until the numbing corrects, and then tighten it.
