Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not loosen him until 20 days or whenever it feels right, then he can put his hands on his neck, and let his shoulders be equal, and beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 days or 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and to us of the two there happen few fractures, and it comes only but bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it befits that the patient sit crossed, and be straight before him equally; then put his hand on the board extended, and extend the ministers the bones broken, and put them equal the mirrors, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in .i. sheet of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the palm toward the belly of the hand, then make a sphere of cloths, and command the patient that he tighten it to his broken palm; and then the restraint of a long cloth, and be the splint of thick wood as large as the palm of the hand, and the restraint, as it befits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the outside, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie tightly around the hand, and bandage the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the two hands, if it is a sprain, set it straight as it should; and restrain it with the palm, and if you see fit put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and not move it; and if the fracture is in the other hand, such as the index or one of the others, set it straight, and tie it with the healthy hand that follows; or tie them all together in .i. holding, which is better, or put a splint on top, like a sprain; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the hot, dry abscess, and correct what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is many times broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is thus, one above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then extend each minister his limb evenly; and this is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, then one limb should be towards the heel, and the other limbs below the fracture. Also, if it is near the knee, then one limb should be near the knee, and the other extension down; then place the splint bone evenly with its two hands, as long as it is according to its natural figure, and then put on the plaster, and bandage, unless an abscess comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and your cure; the bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you envelop upon the fracture .i. with a hard band doubled in .ij. or .iij., and remain the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put .i. long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and let the chief of the thread go upwards; then turn up the leg and up the hip the band, then put upon the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the space between the leg and the hip with cloths to make equal the tightening, then begin to tie firmly .iij. or iiij. above the fracture; and as much as it goes higher above the fracture, the less you tighten it; then hold as .ij. ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and tie .iij. splints which are above, then raise down to the bottom to the chief of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten, so that it does not move from its place, then let it be so, so that there comes no abscess or swelling nor any other semblance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it, and address what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then it is necessary to put them together, if one can; and if one cannot, then it is necessary to cut the space open, and drain pus; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no times is broken the hip in this way that one puts splints, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, with this restoration made it does not cause pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the fracture is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is not more than a split, or one perforation, and it has all wounds, and no wound, and this is well felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is as follows: it is made equal to that which is broken in its two parts, until they are assembled as much as possible; then put the splint, and on it a round piece of wood, if you have need, and bind it as necessary, then follow all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as hot poultices and similar things;  and apply to each accident what is fitting, until he be healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, because one is called 'mustelz' on the right, and the other is called 'foscile'; and all fractures come as it comes to the arm, and for that reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the smaller bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and turns downwards. Then administer extension, and place it even, and bind the splints evenly; but nevertheless, it befits if the fracture is bad, and there are more pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the splint according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have accomplished your work, take two pieces of wood that reach the leg on one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap in two lengths one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this juncture the leg cannot decline to right or left, and thus it is well; and no one administers one splint along the length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and put on the leg to ward off movement, and properly made in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; so cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but the bones of the foot come sometimes fractured and to the two bones, and there have been only a few cases in more dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there comes the bones of the foot fracture, and you see these bones overlap each other, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, then put now your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they return in their places; then put the plaster and bandages above, and put under the belly of the foot a small board at .ij. finger-widths wide, then restrain the foot firmly, then that you have wrapped cloths around, and other things which you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days will have passed, untie the bandage, because you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, return them, as we have said about the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be one point wider, then put under the foot that table that I said, and strain it well; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and strain the table under the foot; and let it stay on the top of the table above the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and secure each accident as it is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, make her sit with her legs spread apart, then incline her toward the back part, and hold her back; then fill the woman's opening with cotton, and put in as much as one stone; then take out the woman, and lift her back up little by little, and then push the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do so for seven days or a little more; thus the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a sheep's bladder, and tie it to the opening, and put the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the bladder until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the arm of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures near are not hidden from those who put their study and use into them, and read my book. For the fracture signifies in more dispositions the right way of restoration: therefore understand.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and put it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until healed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the wounds that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then the retention of vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes to you, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it neither on the third nor fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident upon it.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing above the uncovered heart, then it behooves you to put it gently in place with your hands, little by little.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not available for you to put it in place with your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, which is .vii. or .viii. long, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary for the smith that he forge .iii. or .iiij., according to what he needs for each case of fracture; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend at the compression on the limb in your work, and let it be acute in front and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which the curved head should be placed on the top of the exposed bone; and push it once, so that it returns, and let them be equal to each other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grip the bone, then you must chop the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incision or saw, to your power; then remove that which remains in the bone of asperities and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Then do as long as it is in its place, then moisten one cloth in black spiced wine, and properly if it is in this state; and do not put on the wound cerote or anything else where there is oil, so that it does not cause rot and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and give good guard that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times have fools done this wrong, and have brought upon the patient either death or corruption at any time; and let the strapping be softer and more gentle than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will come from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it does not behoove to put splints; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two begin to bulge at the wound, remove that which you have put on top with all wine, and put healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is joined and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a manner that the bone aligns gently downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the next day it does not join more and returns back askew, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you cover the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the place or any other manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in its chapter before this one. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder, and similar ones of the large limbs, do not try to set it, because many times death comes from it; but leave it until it mends itself, perhaps after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you are able; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of boils which come out of the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is a ugly thing to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps cannot make the members their natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take ward then if it is fresh to us: if it administers topical medicines like aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acaica, and similar others, as you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stimulating wine or with egg white or with a mixture; and put them on the wound in poultices, and restrain it well, and do not loosen it for days; and then release it, and begin another one, until the swelling is gone; or you strain it on a piece of wood well made; because the properties of the wood are that it removes all the swellings from the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above, and make the superfluity appear; or you reapply it to any razor, until it is removed, and cure it as long as it is healing.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and afterward the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tight, and it was not bound as it should; or because there were too many bindings, and it cannot come to the nourishment of the limb; or for multitude of dressings; or for too much movement, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and leisure; then put wax on the limb, so that the wax attracts great nourishment, and the dressing often of water boiled, until the nourishment comes to the limb; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and the torture are fresh, then it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of vismalve, and roots, and melilote, and similar things; and the you .i. make a mollifying plaster, such as dyaquilon well made, and you take the moss of vismalve, and cook it with fat of geline or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or you take fig fats, and grind them with chaff of colon, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And no time is removed the nodes by continual and long rubbing with wet hands. And be administered movement to the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosities are old and hardened, as well as stone, and needs be to remove it with iron, then it is necessary to cut up to the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and put care and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	A dislocation is an issue from a joint out of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is ill-figured, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it is now necessary to bring it back without setting a splint.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, it swells the limb, and by chance if one puts it back with pain in place; for this reason, one should not move it for the hour that it is swollen: many times it brings pain and other aches.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this happens, if you make the patient healthy, then let him, until the abscesses are all appeased; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then move it gently, and cure each member as the wound comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are a little bit moved from their places, and softened a little; or they are dislocated entirely, and hang toward the cheek, and cut off the saliva of the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by the arm's more numerous disarrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it carefully, and do not despair;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the sick person, and put one hand's fist into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be outside, to make it even; and command the sick person to soften their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fist put it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is broken when reset, even if it is the two jawbones together, apply hot water and oil, until they are gently moved; do not hesitate to reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed without softening, put on a soft cloth made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with soft ligatures.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two pillows so that he does not move them to the right or left, nor does he try to chew, but eat light food until the pains are gone, and the jawbones have set.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then gently move what he wants, and don't work on opening his mouth to eat and drink, as long as the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set in place within an hour, and are not converted to their places, then fever and customary fits come, and perhaps a bellyache, and perhaps a thick cold vomit.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these things, then know that it is a death sentence; and many times those who have it die in 8 days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from within the side of the ribs, and it is dislocated no times on the outside, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies quite on his back, and extends his arms; and then presses the place with the shape of your palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head which is towards the rib cannot dislocate; if it does not, and if it dislocates no times, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way is brought back the head of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is that it is dislocated to the side of the seat below; and the second is to the side of the armpit; and by chance it is dislocated above, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it is not dislocated behind the shoulder, nor inside towards the nerves; and many times dislocated below towards the seat, especially in those who have little flesh, because to these it goes easily; in those who have enough flesh, it goes with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with a hot abscess, and thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary for you to examine it thoroughly until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it is pulled towards the hip, and puts a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the hip towards the touch of the top of the shoulder, as if it were one piece; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly at the touch.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this way of dislocation is not otherwise to bring back, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person up, then put their fingers under the armpit, and lift the joint with force upward to its place; and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upward, then put it down; so it will come back little by little.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have said in a few days later, then it is necessary that the sick person be bathed in hot water; and the minister a soothing ointment and softening, like decoction of aloe and fenugreek and melilot in water, and be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then be supported the sick person on his back, and put under the armpit a cushion of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the cushion, and lift the head of the shoulder carefully, and pull the hand of the sick person;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and other ministers hold the head of the patient, so that it does not move down; that shoulder returns all now, and if you see so you reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that you make present one man who is larger than the patient; and be right toward the ribcage, and put his shoulder under the ass of the patient, and lift the ass up, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and other ministers pull the hand of the patient down toward the belly. And if the patient is too light, so you can put with him any thing heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And reset it also in another manner: and is one long stick in earth, whose head be as well round like a pistol, and not too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then be placed under the patient, but he has a sheet above, and the patient is standing on the long shaft of the stick; then his hand is extended down from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take one splint of two arms and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded so as to enter through the hole below the shoulder, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie above the head of the stick sheet below, so that the stick does not hurt the patient, then put it under the shoulder of the patient; and extend his arm up on the long shaft of the stick, and tie the shoulder on the shaft, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on one rung of a ladder of the wide, and let the hands down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in any manner that it may be, then you must put under the shoulder a sphere of wool equal, then put the emplastrum prepared of powder of the mill, with incense and auburn of egg, upon all the shoulder and around, then restrain under the shoulder evenly, and turn the linen upon the emplastrum, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move little, as long as the limb is fortified, because it will heal faster; and then move more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is stiffened and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come or for another cause, then it is necessary that you administer cautery at 3 punctures, as it is laid out in the chapter of cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is severed or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the hip, and the breasts, or behind, it is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and it administers on another place; and care until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain in the limb, and slowness of movement, then use the patient bath many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated in many ways, and returns in many ways; and if it is dislocated from all sides, even before and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, because it is seen well and felt well; and dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the injured rib with the healthy one, if it is well seen. Because the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in the way that abscesses come. Because if abscesses came to it, it would be grievous to return it; and by chance it cannot be returned completely at all, even when it is behind. It is worse than other dislocations and causes greater pain, and death may come from it by chance.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is like this, when it can be brought back, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and his arms be spread out, and the hands do look according to the cut around, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and firm of the root of the palm the cut which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each side, then when you have enveloped a double cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the mire at the joint to his hand, if the oil of any oil to soften the joint, then put the joint formed, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, if put on a dry plaster with yolk of egg, and strain it formed, and bend the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well aligned, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain after resetting the joint, and it moves, then bathe him and rub well, and press until he is soothed; or put on the joint a fleece of fat wool, then leave it for i day and night, then remove it, and let him enter into a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the bandage back on, and then go into the bath; and do so .ii. times or .iii., until he is healed; and if you see, then put on wool fleece moistened with warm butter, and strain over it; it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than the other joints. However, it must be returned to its place carefully, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the limb does not become inflamed, or that there comes a hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is that you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places his hand flat, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, it is necessary that you look if it is well in place; then place the sick person's back of his hand on a table at extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then place the sick person's back of his hand on the table, and he puts his hand on the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, that's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then bind with soothing ointments and poultices the abscess, and leave him so without restarting it.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back in place after some days, the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And does not harm the patient further than while the hand is numb, and cannot extract anything at all: therefore know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; if there is no other means but to constrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is worth nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then constrain it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	No time are dislocated the fingers of the hand on each side, no time on the back of the palm or on the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then are the fingers, and put the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and let it for 2 days, and then put it straight on that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and unbind it daily, and make it move, and bind it again tightly; and do this often, until it is tight,
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do the same, if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and also do the same, when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are more than one dislocations, if there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the joints jump out without will, and cannot be held in place, and many times are softened any limb, or the two hips or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the shin moves to four parts; that which moves in the back is called “gilbositez”:
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The cure for it is that you ward off if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or percussion or similar things, the ancients said manners of cures by great words, in which there is no great profit at all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the boil that comes to the breast before, there is nothing healthy.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also the one that comes directly in two sides, and one cannot cure it except for the one properly that comes to the back, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that the patient be stretched on his back in one even place, and have strain under him so that he does not move;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then put one splint at the head on earth forming, and another at the feet, and tie a linen strap under the arms of the patient, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and the minister knowing the bonds, one at the top and the others at the feet, among the two bones
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the splints as we have said, and the minister puts his palms on the spine, forming it, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board three arms long, and place it under the back, and have the patient lie on his side, and put the head of the board under the back, then place the middle of the board on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and place the minister's feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do so with the turning pin that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And that you place 2 stakes at the head of the patient's arm, and toward the feet 2 others, and there be between each stake, a palm's width of space long.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And have in each stake 1 hole where the turnbuckle runs, and let the stakes be firmly in earth, so that they do not move; and between each 2 stakes have 1 turning stake, on which the ligament turns, and have in 2 turning stakes 2 small stakes of a palm's length, to turn the turnbuckle.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then tie the ligament which is among the shoulders to the turnbuckle toward the head, and the other ligament toward the feet to the other turnbuckle, and each of the ministers turns its turnbuckle on all the ligament, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on a drying plaster with abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of 3 inches long, that protects the place of the rib and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a band, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if any thing comes in the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of cork,
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And sometimes there comes the appearance in the rear spine of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocations; and it is the bone which opens, for which one must not have presumption: by chance would come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only as dislocations, and they do not come like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is that when one joins the leg of the sick person with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens the knee of the sick person more than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot double their knee to the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the place which is below swollen with a hot abscess, for that reason because the head of the hip comes here.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to fire, thus is this accident contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it comes before, thus is that he has his leg well according to accomplishment; nonetheless, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it comes behind, thus is that he cannot expand his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the hip is at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this kind of dislocation is that you observe if the dislocation is old and it remains according to its position, then there is no need for treatment; and it does not behoove him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of the 4 manners of dislocation, so hurry that you return the joint, and its length inside and outside, and the movement to right and left; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must apply 1 strong minister, and extend the leg strongly with 2 hands, or with 1 linen that is tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he pushes his hands below his shoulders, then tightens it with a linen band across the hip; and another holds the head of the linen;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And stretch upwards and downwards at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remain suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If it is not so, then care must be taken to its resemblance. When the dislocation is at the back of the body, you should set the patient on his healthy side, then put a sling under the root of the hip, and where it is below the anger, then extend the sling upwards towards the anger, and towards the shoulder;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then grab with other ministers his arms, and embrace the large part of the injured hip, and extend it outwards in this form: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot bind it in this manner that we have said, then it behooves you to tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick limb be extended two spans more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then be suspended by the top of a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers hanging with the sick person, who embrace firmly the hip, because the jointure now returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the back, let the sick person lie down, as we have said in one who has gout, and restrain one band on the sick limb properly, and on the foot also;
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two sticks, one at the head and one at the feet, then place a stick between the thighs of the patient in the shape;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have planted with drapes moistened around him so that it does not bleach the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and his eyes put equal in his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, it is good. If not, put him on a table and press him as we have said in the chapter on dislocations, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put his pain on the painful side with his hands, then press with the other hand, and the end towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the patient down or raise up the land, but rather he should be as though the hip was dislocated in the back, as we have said about childbirth on the two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And he should be on his face, and the tie extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	And it will be in place when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; therefore adjust the hips, and put on the splint, and the restraint of a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And he rests for 3 or 4 days, then unties it, and puts on the splint again; and if you see that they are even, restrain it as before, and let him rest for 3 days; then unties it, and allows him to walk well, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if he does not rest at his hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as much as he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your two, then bend the two bones that make up the knee; and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he will feel his leg lightly to his hip;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and put the plaster on top, and make the leg rest at the hip, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then untie it; and let the patient not work to go, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not right, then administer strong extension, as we have said in the cure of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of it is that the ankle is swollen, and tender in front at the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction of it is light, and one should extend it gently with his hands when it is only bruised.
